And if there is a need to prick on the face of the foot, you should use all the cautery that is called "point". And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you should use cautery on each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries on each part, all with olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand against it longer than until the skin of the joint is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, then administer the cautery that we have described in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, prick around the wrist 2 lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, then prick each joint and the hair on the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good treatment for the patient and take medicines. For if you make good treatment for him and purge the flux, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rut of the syphilis
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rut comes in the armpits, and the testicles descend into the scrotum, which is new, then when you see it being cured, he should not eat that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts come out of his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his armpit until the testicles are repaired, and bring them up to your fingers, and sign underneath the rut on the bone of the arm, and all over a mark that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is made:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and it feels hot. Then bring the testicles back to their place; and the minister holds his hand so that they do not return; and work well on the armpits of the patient, and put underneath him 1 cushion and 1 servant on the armpits, and another one under the penis which holds his hands; then put the cautery over the mark with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the testicles do not come out when you are doing the cautery; so that he does not burn himself; and so that through this the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you should know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And the cauteries of children should be smaller according to their ears, and those of large people also large according to them; after 3 days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the scorch is removed; then cure it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well sewn up; and it is necessary that their testicles be tied for a long time, so that the testicles do not come out when they start to move around in bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .40 days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another .40 days; and let him have good rest, move little, and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of too much loud speaking; and when he does this instruction, he is completely healed. And I will say hereafter about the cure of cutting in his shoulder.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture in the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are not growing any more, do to him .1 cautery of the fire cautery according to its quantity, and burn it at the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one must cauterize it with a cautery at .3 angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the place of entry and draw a line along the width above the rupture, and another across, and hold your hand in the middle of the cautery. But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or wounding, and the pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then cauterization is needed with a cautery called "point," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its condition of twisting and pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, do another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it must change in the limb nearest to it, so you should do cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The head is sometimes cauterized for great aid, and so are diseases that come from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it cauterized, take care if the disease is in its early stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not lessen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then do 5 cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the corners, and one behind on the nape; and let your hand be so that the cautery comes to the bone, and as long as the skin issues forth so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue out; and cauterize it according to how it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the infection is scattered everywhere; and it is obviously losing ground, then you should cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large cautery on the croup and another smaller one, and two cauteries on the two shoulders; and two cauteries on the elbows, and two cauteries on the tendons of the feet, and one cautery on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the heel so that you do not burn them; and sometimes a cautery is done on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and one more on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And you should know that the more cauteries you do, the more help you provide, and it benefits; and you should know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And the cauteries should be large or small depending on the members and joints, according to how you find them in the methods of the irons. After this, treat the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but it does not heal, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be slightly penetrating into the depth of the skin. Then treat it with ointments until it heals. Sometimes cautery is performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should undertake this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the paths of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albaria
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaria" appears, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a moderately deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then treat it with an ointment made from equal parts of linseed and lentil flour, rose oil, and plantain leaves, plus blood from a black hen and blood from an almond tree. Mix everything together and apply it to the affected area, keeping it in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre. And yet wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet I do not think this is good, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen sometimes; and a more direct thing is to cauterize it all around, with a cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease that is called  "adubelati", and it takes a long time to heal, either due to the excess fluid it produces or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, very old) and have little blood, or due to the season; and you see it needs to heal quickly: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it as it is. For it will heal more quickly.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through, then heat the cautery from which its form comes:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it throughout his body in such a way that the course of the pustule is alleviated. After the cautery, let him heal perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another type of disease called "corrodens", which is simply a corruption of the limb, for it corrodes the limbs just as fire dries up withered branches. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cauterization with fire, then heat the cautery tools, both small and large, according to what is appropriate for the location of the disease; then cauterize all over until you have reached all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and apply a poultice made with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption is removed. After that, treat it with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that no new flesh has grown, then restart the cautery process on any part that still shows signs of corruption. This type of disease can sometimes be treated with medicine instead of fire cauterization; however, fire cauterization is generally more effective. I have already described how to treat the disease with medicine in the corresponding section. Administer it whenever needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of sores that appear on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that in the feet, because of a defect, there arises a disease which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large growth that disfigures the foot. And the cautery for this disease is according to two methods: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that you heat an iron needle as big as a quill pen, made of good steel to the size that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and which has thin edges; then you place it hot on the nail and move your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it starts to produce pus. Then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will drop off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment, gradually hardening it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they appear on the body and many times in the hands and feet, then you should treat them with hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take a brass or iron needle, or a quill pen, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is, the hard skin; then put the needle on so that it bleeds all around, then apply a little hot water, and hold your hand steady and press your hand as you turn it so that the edge of the needle reaches the root of the nail, and thus find the hot water a deep path to the root. Let the patient endure the pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots. Do this one after another, until you extract all those on the body, then cure them with ointments that promote hardening.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is shaking from the coldness of their nerves, or from quartan fever or other [illness], you should make 4 or 5 cauteries on the spine in the back, one cautery between each spinous process; and one cautery on the penis, and one over the stomach with an olive-oil cautery; it will stop the shaking and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes pustules appear all over the body, or foul pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter. One should cauterize each head of the pustule at first sight: with a thin fir twig, whose tip has been taken to the fire, or with a long root of aristologus, or with a lentil-shaped cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this way, and they cannot grow from thereforth, but the superfluity from which they come is disrupted, and they are healed; but this should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are many times great flowings of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery on the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless, when this happens to someone, you must hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly so that the blood is quietened beneath your finger and no drop issues forth; then prepare several olive-wood cauteries, small and large according to the wound and the location where the artery is severed, and place the cautery upon that vein where you are holding your finger, and keep it there until the bleeding is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds afresh when you lift your finger from the wound and the cautery goes out, then quickly take another of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to apply these one after the other until the bleeding is staunched; and be careful not to harm the nerve which lies nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well-staunched by itself when the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have described: by cautery, or by extraction if it is not treated, or by strong ligature with thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to staunch blood; and it should be bound and pressed firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers a tightening of bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not help much if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and there is no medicine or surgeon present, then one should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and tighten it well above the wound and above the vein; and move it not, but moisten it with cold water often so that the blood may become congealed and thickened and tightened; and make inquiries meanwhile about what he needs for cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cauterization with fire, or with burning medicines, and the wounds and causes, and the instruments and forms of cauteries; and I went through that chapter from head to toe, and I will go through this one in the same way so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, my dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish. Because people come to cures in many different ways: some are so distressed by their illness that they would easily be cured if it were not for their stubbornness, and because of the seriousness of their illness; and one must fear these people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these there are some who give you their trust and say, "Wait, I am healed"; but their illness is stubborn. You should not listen to those who approach you in this way, but instead place more importance on your honor than on your desire, and do not act foolishly but wisely in what you know for certain, and in what you can learn and experience; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of illnesses from which salvation is sought. This will help you achieve a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to be inspired by the holy breath of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have instructed you in this chapter by speaking about chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have described to you from the head to the feet, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to infants when they are born, and when the birth canal is too narrow for the child; and sometimes it comes from a cause that we do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease in adults, and in all cases I have observed, death has resulted; therefore, it seems best to me to leave the treatment for another day.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child whose head was swollen with fluid, and the swelling increased every day until it could no longer support itself; and the fluid was so abundant that it reached up to the brain, between the brain and bone, and the treatment for this is such that if the fluid is between the brain and bone and the abscess is small, you should make a large incision in the head, as wide as two fingers, until all the fluid has drained; and here is how you will identify spatulum:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is deeper and the abscess larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the fluid is under the bone and you see the creases of the scalp opening in all directions, and the fluid drains out when you press on it with your hand, and this does not alleviate the condition, then you must make three incisions in the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all moisture firmly. After that, squeeze out the fissures with rags and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound by tenting and poultices, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat, as much as the moisture can bear, until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the size of the abscess opens, and the gathering of the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and where the pus gathers, and open it according to what you can; and beware that you do not cut the artery, and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and the medicine does not help, then the final treatment is cauterization with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them cut, the patient should face away from you; then rub the area around the eyes with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then squeeze the neck of the patient with all your might using a 1-inch cloth; then look where the vein bleeds, and the places are just below the ears, and are very close to each other; then mark the spots, then cut both with a sharp spatulum two parts deep so that the vein reaches the bone, and this should be done from the side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, slicing as deep as two beans across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will jump out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then cut down and slice to the bone; and that which it is necessary to let blood out is six parts, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if any pus remains on the bone, so that the hot abscess does not come there, then drain the wound and ligature it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of emetics
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-age dementia comes, and there is catarrh, due to moisture from tears, and heat in the temples, and old-age forgetfulness, and similar things, and it is not helped by remedies through methods of medicine, then we must cut into the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of its extraction is that the patient pulls back the hair from his temples, and feels for the artery in the temple, which pulses strongly, especially in those who are too cold; and if it is not pulsing strongly, the patient should hold a warm water-soaked cloth to the area until it does. Then take the spatulum, of which there is a description below:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scorch the skin slightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with tweezers, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath it in each part; and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the fingernail, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two fingers. For if it is not cut, the blood will not flow throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from 1/4 to 3/8 of an inch; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound heals, and that blood comes out freely; then cut off the excess between the two ligatures in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron knife up to the bone until the shoulders are cut; and this is the main course of treatment if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to dry up moisture, that is why it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the site with old cotton and places it on well-made bandages; and when they are removed, they should be healed with dry medicines that cause scabs to form, and with bandages until they are healed; and if without cutting through the artery as much as you operate, you hasten to cover it by cauterizing, or you employ vitriol and strain it in your hand so that the blood is stained; and if you do not have that present, you place your finger on the site so that the blood congeals, and wet the site with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as it should be; and what is better and easier for the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of two parts, but the cutter should be quite thick in order to retain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the body is too weak, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives a distance of one finger's width, and then when you have cut through both sides, you place the hot iron over it until it reaches the bone, and you close the vein in two places; and the two heads should be separated because they are not fused by this cautery from top to bottom; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are flowing from the veins that are above the testes in the head, and it does not help to use medicine on it, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and he feels heat or burning in his forehead, and his eyes are weak and moist so that the hair of his eyelashes has fallen out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancient ones called it "curing contusions," and you should do to the patient who has this disease that he has hairs on his forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as two fingers all across the forehead from above, and the other two at two sides over the temples, and be careful not to cut into the arteries which are at the two sides over the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the width of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a piece of sponge and some gauze to wipe up the blood, then pour into the wound the spatumile made of two parts of oil and one part of vinegar:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is towards the temple all the way to the second incision; and burn all the skin which is between the two cuts up to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you pour into the first cut the instrument which is called  "culter", and is very sharp on one side, and not sharp at all on the other, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the incision towards the chest and the armpit to the heart, and the other one towards the bone, and open it until it reaches the middle incision. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to the one that opens into the heart, and then make another incision in the middle up to the other defiant; then extract equally of blood and express the site for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and place moistened sheets in wine and oil and garlic, and guard against hot abscesses coming; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer a large amount of warm water, then treat with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a constant runny nose, and you see the eyes are pale and sunken, and the vision is weak, and the eyelids are burned, and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come from many veins, and the medicine that cures it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should command the patient to bend his forehead, then make a large slit in the middle of the forehead, and another one from the left temple to the right, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control swallowing; when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two lips of the slit and insert old cotton, and apply tenting with linen; then bind moistened rags in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, you should rub the bone until new skin begins to grow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote the formation of new skin.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same way: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds to promote the formation of new skin throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the treatment of ear infections:
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or animals, or stone, or similar objects like iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans, and peas; or flowing substances, such as water and garlic, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone falls into the ear or another object that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in it, hold the ear towards the sun. If you see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or oil of assafety, and then administer extraction; and make the patient sneeze with snuff, and stop the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear upwards. Often it comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine tweezers, which have this shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with tweezers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine needle of small diameter; and if it does not come out through this, make an iron hook and insert the tip of the hook into the ear canal firmly, and stop the space around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out directly, for often it comes out in this manner as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a way, take some glue and place it on something pointed suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have mentioned, then be quick to split the ear so that the abscess and pain subside, and the method of splitting is that you first bleed the patient's head and extract blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fatty tissue where it depends; and the split should be like a crescent moon, so that you can reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it energetically with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains within it and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue out, then administer a .i. spatumile tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with subtle tweezers and a suction cup, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the acute condition that affects the ear, the patient should use a nose-pack made of suitable materials, and fill the ear with soft cotton. And he should lie down on the affected side. If the water comes out through the nose, that is good. If not, he should take several thin stones according to the size of his nostrils, heat them, and place one nostril in the ear, and press down on it with another stone; and keep doing this with different stones until all the water comes out, as we have said for the stones. And if you see that, take a straw and insert one end into the ear, and hold the other end to his nose; and squeeze his nostril until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an object from the ear, if it is a small object, such as a louse or something similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section. But if it is a large object that can be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and it is the easiest thing to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat it as we have described in the section on distilleries, and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, you should pluck them out with a pair of delicate tweezers. If none appear, take a piece of wool from where they are formed.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. And insert its most delicate end into the ear according to the amount of suffering caused by the disease; then suck firmly on the entire wool. Repeat this frequently until all the worms come out. If they do not obey and emerge, stop up around the cotton as I have said about stones; if they do not come out as we have described, administer distillation remedies which the ancients have experimented with for worm removal, and you will find them in the section on distillations; distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, from where the worms are formed.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a narrow end having one small hole and a wider top for distillation; to press the distillation into this instrument, use a well-crafted brass tool, and if you see fit, take a razor and wrap the tip with cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and what remedies you wish from your medicines into the wool, and let the wool be in the ear; then insert the razor over all the cotton, and gently press your hand so that the oil is distilled into the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warmed by fire so that it is not too cold when distilled into the ear.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of earache
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to earache, or an injury inside the ear. Sometimes these openings occur in the ear itself, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a small wound at the opening of the ear, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when the opening occurs and is not visible, it is due to a grievous wound in various parts, and in such cases one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane exposed, then examine it closely to understand its shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointy at the front and back, so that it does not cut or injure the ear; if the membrane is due to a wound in the body of the ear, then grasp it with fine tweezers and gently peel away this wound.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the infection is deep in the ear, take a thin, lightweight razor, heat it slightly in the fire, and then place it on the body of the ear. If you feel the infection that the patient feels when listening, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert a tent into the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is closed; then take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is appropriate to pull out the tent and move another tent moistened with cerot made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding that are in the remedies for distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the char of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This herb when it comes in papers of itself when they are moist and are dry, you must extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the root of a spatula; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without peeling, then cauterize it with a thin lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision heals scabs; and many times they return, as long as something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in papers of things that look like hail in shape and hardness, and this is why the disease is called "hailstone", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on top and bottom; the work is as follows: take care if the hailstone breaks from one side to another, and it is a minor thing to know; they then open it with tweezers, and peel it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it will not harm the patient; and if the crack is large, there is a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will restore it immediately and heal the wound.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and grip the hailstone with pincers, and squeeze it from both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, that does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, apply a poultice of salted water, and clean the wound of any foreign matter until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat which is woven into the paper above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it causes great harm to their eyes, and they experience catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because the tears rush to their eyes; and because of this, they lie down on their faces and sleep, and their eyelids become moist which inflames and covers the appearance of the exinach. And when you press the area with your fingers, it seeps out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient places his head on the operator's lap; and then take 1 linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that the exinach occupies in each part, and then place it over the eye; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle; then cut through the moist skin with a spatula, making an incision no larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and in various cases, the exinach comes out of the incision in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take therefore a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and twist your hand from right to left until it is taut; and be careful not to push into the fissure so that you do not go all the way to the eye, lest you blister it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the skin opens at the beginning of the fissure, gently spread the fissure slightly so that it appears; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloth in vinegar and water, and place on the area, and draw out with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who bruise it and put something on it to corrupt that moisture which remains. Then treat the wound until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes in the area, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.Et s’il vient aposteme froid, si le cure d’emplaustres chautes qui sont assouajans, tant qu’il soit sanez.
des poilz des papieres	of hair of parchment
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers other than their natural place, and they are enveillit, they harm themselves and bring on various diseases, just as tears, softening of the paper, and albugine, until it leads to their destruction; and there are four ways to treat this: through cauterization with fire, or with a medicine water according to what is mentioned before the chapter on cauterization, and either through incision and stitching or through splints, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the head of the patient in your lap, then hold the paper of the eye in your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, then thread a needle with .i. thread; and this should be done from the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and draw .i. thread over the entire paper, and return to the razor; then cut into the part under the paper, under the awkward hairs, to the spatumile, copant, from the large larmier to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and cloth underneath the paper, then sign over the paper a figure of an inch, like a fuelle of mirte, and still it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see rising up in every part.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut out a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper has become, then cut into the spatumile over the two lines you have marked and begin from the large larmier to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert an awl into one of the angles of the eye socket, then scrape it all off; then bring together the two lips with a stitch using an needle and thread made of fine wool, and draw out the blood, and allow any excess thread to hang over the two eyelids, if you wish to do so; and if not, then leave the stitch and threads for 3 or 4 days, then treat the wound without a stitch using dry and constricting things, because the paper lifts up around the wound and by bringing it together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients say), and this work is done without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another way: and that you draw the paper with a figure that is also like the leaf of the myrtle, as we have told, to .I. inches wide according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small scissors evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the object is not even, then take a needle with which you have .I. thread, and pierce it through the figure; and take another thread from the large vein, and the second thread from the small one, and bring together the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have signed, as we have told, then bring together the .ij. lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes the hair of the paper is inverted: so you should use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing in one and another is more artificial.
