Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the cane is as follows: you must first turn the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two canes by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spathomyle; then tie two pairs of threads where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly above what is on top of the paper of the eye, and pull out the two canes from the two formed parts; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that was stretched will die and harden and fall off, as long as it falls through itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow, if the cope exerts some force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sutured, and if the paper is raised, the hairs will no longer grow there; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the operations are such that you pierce a needle and insert a fine and subtle silk thread; then join the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the eye, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in your hand; and let it be exposed to sunlight so that the operations are declared, for this is a subtle and fine operation, then insert the needle into the root of the hair near the skin, and pierce the paper obliquely until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the thread and insert it into the eye of the needle with the natural hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs come out straight through the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you shall treat the wound underneath to the very end that you have prepared for it, until the wound comes out through the opening above and you see it with your eye; then you shall treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, then accompany it with a long hair from the horse's mane, and let it grow with that one which you leave, until it is elongated and then you remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eyelash
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "alacrity" or the eyelash comes in the eye, it has two causes: natural and unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of treatment for this is that you split the wound open, and separate the eyelids, and put in it tents of linen, and bind it up until it heals; and one should not use in its treatment anything that dries and restricts. For if you do, then the disease will return worse than before; but one should use things that soften, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altered water and linseed are cooked, and diaquilon is melted in some of the oils, and it is wrapped up in a tent, and cured like this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is under the eye is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from a wound and from a cut and cautery and similar things; and the way of doing the operation on it is that you take a needle, with which there is a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct so that the threads come out on both sides of the eye, then the flesh above is cut all the way to the needle, and the skin is pulled back about one spathum wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits along the side within the paper; and let the edges of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision which you have cut, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has the number "J" in Greek; then remove this flesh, according to the amount that its sides are bent down below, following along with the paper; then join together the two separated parts, and sew it up with a thread of wool; then cure it as we have said with softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you should make a plain split underneath the hair of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and the operation should be performed according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an instrument with all his power, how he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of operation and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this splitting occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the scalp above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should therefore insert the point of a razor underneath the scalp, and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers, until you grip what is open to the subtile spatula, which is neither too round nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot bear that the too-sharp spatula pierces the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel away this union, lightly, so that the scalp returns according to its natural shape; and all of this union is healed, and they sometimes create an ulcer in the eye, and raise it with warm water, and with a bandage; then place a tent of linen between the scalp and the eye, and place wet wool on the eye; and after the third day, use the bandage and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You should know that the nail comes in two forms: one is nerveous and resembles a hard cyst; the other is not nerveous but resembles congealed white moisture, which, when touched with iron and pinched, cannot be pierced by any means; both kinds begin at the inner corner of the eye, grow little by little, and cover the entire sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head over yours, then he opens his eyes; you hold the piece of paper in your hand, then grip the nail with tweezers at the cuticle and lift it up; next, take a needle, thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox hair through it, double the tip of the needle over, insert it into the nail, tie the nail with a thread, and lift it up; then scrape along the side of the nail that follows the eyelid all the way to the tear gland, being careful to not pierce the tear duct; sometimes, only the cuticle and thread are needed, as mentioned; then scrape along the soft tissue around the tear gland, taking care not to damage the tear duct with the incision.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch the fleshy membrane and rupture it, nor pierce the tear gland; after the incision, apply a little powdered quicklime to the eye, and a collar made of linseed oil, and leave it on until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot push in the needle, and the hooked pins cannot enter, many times this kind of nail has been cured by medicines; and it heals as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the eye of the malady, and take the spatula gently with a small hook according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently, and if you see that it does not lessen and the pus continues to come out, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar, and if it is ground, and stop the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same action, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no contrary thing in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it with milk, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.Se li ungle est vairons ou si grant, et ne puet gueres estre curé, adonques le tranche selonc la forme de l’ungle, et le traie hors dou pie; puis tache l’ungle s’il est chaut, et met sus dou baume de colofonia et d’uncina de vairons et de pluyer, et le retrempe en l’oil dou mal.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the nail is very large and cannot be cured easily, then cut it according to the shape of the nail, and pull it out from the toe; then burn the nail if it is hot, and put on balsam of colophony and of the nail and of vitriol, and re-drip into the eye of the malady.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men sometimes grows red flesh above the eyeball, covering it and pressing against the eyelids, and they turn their eyes upwards, resembling a rose in its bud; and if one puts pressure on the eye of the patient, then he can operate on them, pulling out all the flesh with tweezers as far as possible, and then he cuts through to the bone at the joint where this happens, as described in this chapter, using gentle force to remove the growth; then he cuts away the first piece of flesh, and continues cutting down to the eyeball, being careful not to damage it; and the incision is made as we described for the nail, with small movements so that one can remove the growth, as shown in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then treat the eye with egg white mixed with red vitriol and other corrosive medicines, and cover it with cotton soaked in egg white to protect against hot abscesses; and if anything remains, and the eye becomes sore, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your treatment once the eye is healed, and do this for as long as necessary.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should always use the natural method for curing weak eyes, and the accidental method for strong eyes; and do not use your hand in either treatment until you see that this member is suffering from the other treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	They are red veins that lie over the eye, and they hinder vision and weaken the eye every day. Therefore, first, you must examine the eye, for if there is nothing wrong with it other than the redness, then treat it thus: instruct the patient to tilt their head back so that it lies flat, then gently massage those veins all around the socket according to your wisdom, and make the massage strokes short and quick according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And massage in circles going downward on one side of the eye according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then press those veins gently, and draw out the blood little by little, hour after hour, until you see the veins drawn away from the eye; but be careful not to hurt the eye with the points of your fingers, and do this work at noon in the sunlight, and be very diligent in your task so that you do not leave any of the veins untouched. And when you have finished, instil a mixture of green and red collyrium into the eye to purify what remains of the redness.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to pull out all of this in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and let it be for several days until the pain is appeased and assured of a hot abscess; then begin again according to the manner set forth above until he is healed; and that is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Look carefully at the "arissati" fistula: when you heal it with cautery and medicine with a hot fire according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there is an issue in it that you split open over the abscess, where it should remain, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you will see the corruption and blackness, then you will use the instrument again, of which there is the form; and it is called a  "aspre chief", and it should be made to be sharp at one end, and punctured like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; do this a few times, then restore the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the fistula is not healed and there is no improvement after 40 days, and nothing bad happens, then you can be sure that it has healed; if not, there is only one other thing to do, which is to open the fistula at its opening with a knife according to this form: first, expose the bone again using iron and sharp medicines, then take a small piece of iron according to this form, and make the shaft thin up to the tip as you see here, and make the head into three prongs.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone at the fistula, and move your hand away slightly, then push the entire instrument in until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through their windpipe; then restore the site with dry medicines as I have instructed you before. Once the wound heals and hardens over the site, examine the material at the opening of the fistula; this is a gentler method for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the eye:
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open all around and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you should ligature the patient; then heal, then place leeches or suckers without piercing to draw out, then apply a poultice on top made from aconite and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then bind the eye, using bandages and linen; the manner of the linen is that you fold linen very softly, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind it tightly from above with a firm bandage, and then restart the leeches to draw out without piercing; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the ligature softens, then you should tighten it greatly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then restart the poultice and the linen and the ligature and the leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in woven fabric, then it opens and appears like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below up to the part above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread of the part of the armhole; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the place of the double thread and tie one part of the fabric around, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and apply a poultice made from a soft egg yolk on top of the eye; and leave it until the thread breaks with the fabric, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the fabric in a circle of linen, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great pain, then pierce them with a sharp needle which comes from the back of the eye, and dry out the moist white part and lower the eyes, and put them in as far as they will go; then pull on them until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the back of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is only in the eye, which is assembled in the eye, looking like water, but it is not; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you have the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then hold his head with both hands and move it until you see the bow coming to your eyes; then it must be pierced, and the light must not descend and be obscured, and the patient should see things as he usually does. If the bow does not descend under, know that it is water, and if the bow does not appear as we have said, hold the patient between your hands, then take the sharp needle and pierce through the white part of the eye, through the conjunctiva, into the cornea, until the bow comes out; and when it is issued, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled with honey, and let it be cured with another cure until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearances of the diseases in the division, and what is needed to pierce; then act according to health. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so that the sun does not hurt his eyes, and hold his healthy eye very tightly; then put the paper on your left hand if his eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if his eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if his eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument along the crown by the thickness of a thread in that part of the eyeball where the tear duct is located, then insert the instrument called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand so that it pierces the eyeball, and you will feel that almagda comes to the empty space; and the measure of the path of almagda should reach the bottom of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the horny membrane, and then insert the instrument where the ailment is, then express it from one path to another. If the ailment is flowing now, the patient sees the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the ailment flows back up the second path, push it down with the instrument; and when it is stuck and does not flow, gently withdraw almagda by turning your hand a little bit; then put in the eye a little more sealed silk, and remove it from that eye. Then place on the affected eye, as a poultice, comfrey crushed with plenty of egg, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those of our time, also put on comfrey bruised with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make a small slit, then insert alum, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient a dark chamber in which he can sleep on his back in a dimly lit place; and he must be free from all movement, and eat light foods, and not move his head to the right or left, and he must be bound according to his condition for three days; then release him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then release the bandage by the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should alleviate it so that the water can flow gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	if there are hot abscesses, you should release the eye before the seventh day, and use a remedy that soothes abscesses; and when it is calm, remove the sight and place an eye patch over one eye to cover it, and he should remain in that dark room. Then leave the house little by little, and return to his normal state; and know that no student should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Land of Iraq, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and suck out the water, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similitudes of the forms of almagest, because those who do not know them may see them; and they are properly made of brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the points in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there arise on the nose warts which are diverse, from which it happens that some appear like scorpions with many feet; and also there are those where the wart is indented of a dark color, and others which are protuberant of a fair color. When this occurs in one of these warts which is protuberant and not indented, you should cause the patient to sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, pour the oil upon them, and draw it out with force; then press it as much as you can endure by means of the spatumile which is slender at one end.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If something remains which cannot be removed, then open it with a sharp instrument lightly so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess forms, then lanced as appropriate; and if malignant abscesses form, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the corruption is removed, then apply cold water, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the ear is affected, and moisture extends to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is corruption in the bone above, therefore do not use an instrument to cut: instead, take a thread of linen, about the thickness of a finger, and tie it with a knot at one end, and make intervals between each knot, a digit or less; and let the patient place the thread in his nostril as far as he can bear it, and draw it through until it comes out through the mouth; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wishes to do it. Then hold the end that comes from the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them gently apart in opposite directions until you know that the thread has dislodged the corruption, then remove the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nostril as before. Repeat this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the corruption; and then insert a plug made of cotton wool in the ear for several days until it is healed, and if medicine is needed to dry the ear, then use it. This is the instrument used to cleanse the ears, with which one can draw out oils and medicines through the nostril:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or brass, in the shape of an open lamp, like a tube, and with a handle to control it; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and fill it with medicine to cleanse the ears; and there should be a small handle at the end for holding it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the nose; it grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to the eye. Therefore, you should treat it at first, and remove all of it, then place upon it a cautery or burning medicine. If one delays in treating it until it has become large, then be wary if it is hard, dark in color, and insensate: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess. For when one treats it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is due to a superficial touch, not from deep color, and you see that one can completely cover it, then evacuates the patient and treat the site with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a break occurs in one of the cartilage-like bones, it benefits only a few people. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then split both lips with one stitch, then cure it until it heals. If the lips are separated on either side, then you should scrape all parts of their edges until they heal, then sew the two lips together with a stitch, and tighten them, and powder them with powdered dragon's blood and incense; and place a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster over the powders, and let it stay in place until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the needle: either by needle, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home on the lips there are hard abscesses, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; therefore you should cut into the lip, and pierce each pustule with pincers, and scrape out each one; then apply powdered vitriol after making an incision, until the blood is stopped; then use a poultice of garlic, and treat the area with dry remedies until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum pain
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow out; then place ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cautery, that is the form for treating an abscess.
des sordens	of the ears, and of the eyes, and of the nose, and of the throat, and of the mouth, and of the gums, and of the teeth, and of the tongue, and of the palates, and of the head, and of the brain, and of the neck, and of the collar bones, and of the shoulders, and of the armpits, and of the arms, and of the elbows, and of the wrists, and of the hands, and of the fingers.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the roots of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, scabs that are unsightly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and wormy, when corruption comes to the gum, and they stink; so you should make the patient hold his head in your hands, and press his gums with your thumb, and pull the teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and thus do the same for blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other discoloration, until they are cleaned; and if one pulls out what is at the first cause, that is good; if not, then repeat it again on the second day and the third, until you have pulled everything out; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for pulling, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the instrument used to pull out teeth have different forms from those used to pull between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache and draw it out, take as long as you can, for this must not be done quickly; for the tooth is a very sensitive substance until there is no more excuse for drawing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw it out, you must be certain which tooth it is that hurts. Often the pain deceives the patient and he thinks that the tooth that hurts is a healthy one, so he draws out the good tooth; yet the pain is not relieved because of this, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have already seen this happen to some patients; and when you are certain which tooth it is, you must cut around the tooth all the way to the gum; then press hard with your fingers or with small pincers all around the tooth until it is well loosened, then grip it firmly with the pincers; and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After drawing out the tooth carefully without breaking it, if it will not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it into each side of the tooth gently and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced or decayed, you must fill its holes with wax, and then grip it firmly with the pincers so that it does not break when you pull; and you must work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part of it behind, and bring back greater pain to the patient through the malice of its root, for sometimes ignorant surgeons, in their haste and arrogance, break teeth, and do not use what we have instructed; but they sometimes bring on great illness because of this, either through the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine, or garlic and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which the teeth are pulled first should have long points and thick handles so they do not break when you pull on the tooth. And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of strong metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should have teeth to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in while pulling, you should put moist cotton on the spot for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then, use tweezers called "algefri", which make the gums look like a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is to say, a spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be strong and wide so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two branches, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of others; and if it does not break in the cart or other bones, but protrudes, then he looks for the instruments that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural structure of the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then cut it off; and if there is an air bubble with the tooth, then take this instrument of which the form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharpened at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum shrinks a little bit each day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, then file it with an ivory file like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth a little bit each day lightly, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file the sharpness so that it is even and does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, by удар or by falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without them coming out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it does not work; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never moves; and let the wire be medium or thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you want to direct the teeth, take the wire and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the head between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, as long as you come to the bleeding part on the other side; then start again at the point where you applied pressure, and hold your hand firmly and gently so that it does not move. Then wrap the wire around the teeth with a pair of tweezers, and assemble them, and tie them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not cut the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone or the wire breaks, then tie it with another wire. It will remain like this and serve for all time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of how to direct the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and careful should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and placed in the place where there is a defect, and bound as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the line on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this line comes from under the tongue as a natural birth defect, and sometimes it is caused by an injury; and the treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, and press their head towards your hand, and lift their tongue; then cover the nerve line from the side, so that the tongue is loosened from its socket. And if there is hardening due to injury, cut it from the side as well, and make sure the incision isn't too deep so as not to cut the artery underneath. Once you're done, apply a mixture of rosewater and garlic, or just cold water, and then place a linen tent under the tongue; and every night, treat the wound with an ointment made from lard and honey, so that the wound does not heal closed. If bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol; and if the bleeding continues, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Then clean the wound further until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is dark colored or black and hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a ulcer; and if it is inclined towards gangrene, and there is moisture, cut it from the side with a sharp spatula, and loosen it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your action, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment, pulling out all the way, then apply a mixture of garlic and vinegar, and clean the wound further until it heals. Then apply a poultice of garlic and vinegar to the affected area, and clean the wound further until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are sometimes swellings inside the throat called "godath," and they are properly called tonsils. And when you treat them as described in the previous section, if they do not heal, pay attention to the following: If the abscesses are hard, small, and of a purplish color, do not touch them with iron. If they are red and the root is swollen, do not use iron either, so as not to cause bleeding; let it be until it bursts on its own. And if they are white in appearance and the roots are thin, prepare an instrument for cauterization, but first make sure that the abscesses have cooled down and are calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with his head tilted back, his mouth open, and his tongue pressed down by a servant's hand, and apply the cautery instrument, which can be made of silver or thin bronze, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue with this instrument, you will see the abscess; then take a pair of forceps and insert it into the tonsil, pulling it out as far as possible. Remove any threads from the wound with the forceps, then cover the wound with the cautery instrument again, which has a pointed shape, resembling a needle; the instrument should be curved on one side and straight on the other, and very sharp, made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use tweezers, which have a similar shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is pointed on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have lanced one of the glands, lance the other according to the same method, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and garlic, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water or cooked pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two glands form in the throat, so lance them thus as the two glands were lanced.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely, one abscess of small size; and she had almost closed her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one or two days. And the abscesses were already so swollen that they had pushed out two openings from the nose. I hastened, therefore, and inserted an incision into one of them, then drew out a large amount of pus; then I made another incision in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the incision into the abscesses and cut out a portion, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and it would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore, I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left these parts, and I do not know what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye descends into the socket, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an "uve". When it has been incised as we have said in the division, and the incision does not help, and you see that the surrounding abscesses are pacified, and it is delicate, then you should cope with it; and if it is rounded and not long, and is blood-red or the color of pus or black, then you should avoid incising it. For there is great danger in doing so. Therefore, when you see it, according to its whiteness and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the probe into the eye, and draw it out from beneath, and cope with it using one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision of the two almond-shaped eyes. And you should not cope beyond the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit, for if you do, it will harm the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almond-shaped eyes, and treat it until it heals. And if the patient fears having it incised, then you should use a cautery on his tongue without fear. The manner of the cautery is as follows: the patient puts his head against your healthy eye, then presses his tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and breathes against a live coal so that it is not too dense or too clear; and with this instrument, which has this shape,
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and has a handle at the top where one puts the medication, like the handle of a spoon, and places the instrument with all the medication on it over the eye; and the patient should lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth due to the medication inside, so that it does not descend into the throat and choke him; then hold your hand over the medication and press it onto the eye for the duration of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medication calm down. And if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the eye all the way to the cotton, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to re-administer the cautery of the medication, then do so, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamine and hyssop and marjoram and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil.
