And the pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and in the pot there should be one instrument shaped according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it may be made of silver or brass, and the end of one is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; then he is treated again frequently, until the eye dries up; and beware of doing this at the beginning of the occurrence of a hot abscess, for many things happen there; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an egg shell inside it, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg shell will not allow the vapor to burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some object, becomes stuck in the throat; so you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the object; and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you should make the patient vomit as long as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and attach a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the spot, it will stick, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end lifted up high; and beware of touching the epiglottis, so that it does not choke him, nor push the bone inside; and move as long as the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can move the object; then he swallows it down, or pulls it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the blood is healed with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you. And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with тонкими щипцами, which are suitable for this. And if that doesn't work, take a long needle, insert it into the throat of the patient, and then heat the needle, and do this often. And if the disease is caused by water, fill a glass with cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will retract.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not withdraw as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for fumigation of the throat; do this many times, because it will withdraw without bleeding. And the way to fumigate is to place burning charcoal in a pot, and cover the pot with a perforated lid, and insert the end of the instrument into the hole; then blow your smoke into the instrument, and the patient should put the needle into his mouth, close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but go to the blood; and the blood will withdraw immediately, and if it does not withdraw, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and do not drink water; and then he will need to urinate.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids resembles, when it can be seen, bent tongs designed to enter the throat; it also resembles a doctor's beak and has the roughness of a file so that it cannot let go of what it grasps. And here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	for abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, as the following account from various sources in this book shows, and they differ according to their location and size; and there are two main types, those which are in the flesh and those which appear at the joints. Abscesses on the head are different from those on the body's foundations, and those that appear on fleshy parts are different from those found at the joints, each with its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And for abscesses one must not pierce them until the pus has formed and it is ready to drain; but there are some which should be pierced when they are still forming, like those that appear at the joints. For if an abscess appears at a joint, and you leave it until it forms a hard mass, then often the ligament and nerve of the joint will be damaged, causing contraction in the limb. If the abscess is near the main limb, and you delay piercing it until it is fully formed, it will harm the main limb; but if it is near the body's foundation, one should pierce it when it is ready to burst and not let it form a deep pus pocket, which can cause lasting damage. One must not pierce an abscess that has not yet formed pus and is still digesting, except for those that appear at the joints, as these should be drained before they fully form.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to its maturity, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departing of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing at the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears soft; and the piercing should be made deep in the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints, and on nerves, and arteries, and in all places alike where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In places that fold, according to the member. And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the piercing until it is confirmed by completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, then the poison will spread throughout the body from it, and it will be filled with much filth; and perhaps the lips and the depths of it will harden. And for small abscesses, make small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where one should draw out the pus, and cover up; when it has become like a shirt, and is deadened, then one must do as one does with blisters: and there are some that are split in three angles, and some which one covers like the leaf of a myrtle, as with abscesses on the bones; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, as with a superficial abscess, you should pierce it plainly; and when the abscess is large, and has drawn much pus, and you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but some part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this several times until all the pus is out; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an elderly person. For sometimes the wound twitches with the issue of the pus, and perhaps kills the patient, and you do not realize it. Therefore be very cautious about this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, wash the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; if it is a plain incision, then dress it with tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes in it, then put a tent in each one so that they come up against each other; and if you have cut into the skin of the abscess, and drawn it out all around, then fill it with old cotton or rags of linen without moisture, and let it lie for three days; then remove it, and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood flow occurs due to your work, bring cold water and a wet cloth, and place it over the bleeding area multiple times. If the blood flow persists, apply pressure and treatment, and use the powders I have described earlier in this book. If it is winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place warm tents and clothes moistened with wine and oil over the site; if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place moistened clothes with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil, for a third of the day, as we have said. Then cut into the abscess, wash and treat it, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Now you should understand, in general, the treatment of abscesses. I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and you can find this chapter now.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or let us discuss the sores that come from the head, which are like those of mice, and there are many variations. Some are fatty and some are hard and bony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects. The operation of this type is such that you must try every instrument called an 'entromissoire', by which the form comes later, showing what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then it is opened from above. And when the moisture is discharged, then it is peeled without leaving any skin that contains the moisture, for it returns as soon as something is left; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and repeat this process every day until you are sure that nothing remains overnight. Then treat the wound with appropriate ointment, until it heals. And if the abscess contains a fat-like substance, then cut it according to its shape, from above; and squeeze out your fingers, and peel it all over, and put all your treatment into drawing out the pus or fluid; and if the artery causes contrary effects, then do as I have told you after. And also do this for an abscess that is hard and bony in texture, cutting and treating it as I have said before.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a stony and moist abscess is lighter, because they contain little blood. And in some of these abscesses on the head or where there is no moisture, I had an abscess on the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be crushed; and if anyone had broken it, it would have made a wound like a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should be all day in the most dependent place, for the pus to issue; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses come to the neck and under the armpits, and sometimes in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body; and they are numerous, and are connected with each other. And each scrofula is properly within its coat, as the boil and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many kinds of these scrofulae. There are some which contain moisture, and some which are malignant and do not respond to treatment. So when you see one with a good disposition for lancing, and it is similar in color to the rest of the body, and is not swollen anywhere, nor adherent to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you should lance it from above, and scrape each part, and the two lips of the wound should be at an angle, as needed, as we have said for abscesses on the head; and drain it little by little, and be careful not to cut into the nerve or vein, and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut anything you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cauterize the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put into the wound vitriol ground, or any powders that stanch blood, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess is pacified, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester. And when the blood is stanched, return to your task, until you have finished it; then examine with your finger if there remains any small scrofula, and scrape them off and clean them. And if in the root of the scrofula there is a large vein, then you should not cauterize that scrofula in its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through it without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize the whole scrofula, then it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, so that there remains no superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. Then you should proceed to cauterize its root and draw it out, and stitch it as we have said before. Those scrofulae that retain superfluity, pierce where the vein appears; and pierce it in the same way as the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then apply tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, cure it with ointment, causing a blister, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients wrote and spoke of throat surgery; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with scrofula, it is necessary to open the flap of the throat, called the 'epiglottis'; and this should be done gently, for all the veins and the lymph node are affected by the disease, whether the abscess is hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the lymph node channel, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.Il conviant aussi que li medecins sache le goute et le sentour de la maladie; car onque il n’i a pas bon sanz sa science.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is also necessary for the doctor to understand the nature and extent of the disease, for one cannot treat it effectively without that knowledge. Therefore, when we wish to open the epiglottis, we should do so below the third or fourth circle, or with a small slit across the middle, not in the cartilage.et que la fendure soit desoz les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac; et ne fie en la cartillaige. Et s’il avient que li pormon soit en la cartillaige ou plus hault, il faut le fendre en la cartillaige, ou plus hault, selonc le sentour de la maladie.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those who are suitable for the incision of the epiglottis, where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat to the Adam's apple, then cut through the skin as far down as the larynx; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then split the hyoid bone, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated through the incision of the larynx that the breath escapes through the opening, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely choked, and the patient judged to be dead, and the failure of the windpipe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one should grasp the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus be guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the maliciousness of the disease was passed, and it is passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young lady take a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut open the gums of her teeth;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that blood had issued from it; I saw that it had not bled copiously or been directed outward other than through the throat, and the blood had escaped through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened to sew up the wound, and treated it until it healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the lady had no more pain than a minor discomfort, and recovered her strength afterward.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore, I say that one should not be afraid to cut into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess the color of ochre, and it occurs often in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it has two causes: natural and accidental; when it is natural, there is no innate predisposition.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental cause has two forms: one is similar to a swollen hernia, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and he has fear, and one should not work with fire except in that which is small, and test and examine all the instruments:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as smooth as an egg, and cannot get anywhere with it, then chop it up like we do nuts, and scrape the top of its shell if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and examine well all around, and clean it as it should be, until it is perfectly clean.
des nous	of nuts
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways to do this, all of which I will describe.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I shall explain the difference between a dislocation and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is a fever and heat which persists until the effusion has passed and the swelling is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a dislocation, there is no fever or heat or pain, and it contains a pus-filled blister which is the same colour as the body, and begins like a pimple and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, either dry, or moist, and of various colors as I have said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first examine and test it with all the instruments called "introductors," according to what its shape will allow in the following chapters.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses in the nose is that you press on the most moist spot that you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull out the introducer, and take care in what it goes.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If pus runs short, whatever color it has, they should treat it as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the incision no pus comes out, know that it is fatty, so they should make a cross-shaped cut and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side, and guard the coat where it lies so that you draw it out clean with the thread.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out cleanly, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it lingers for a while and the pain is not severe, then treat the wound with some corrosive powders, and bandage the wound, and apply hot poultices to soothe the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it heals;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which causes scabs.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the bleeding vein is contrary or elsewhere, then hurry and apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound scabs over, and rest from the bleeding; then return to applying what was left off earlier.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments for probing, and they come in three types: large, medium, and small; and there are four of them called "albaret", and one called "breb"; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses of fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles used to pierce warts; they are made of brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are just as effective and are more often used with black pitch to encircle the curves of fistulas;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the hooks are very varied, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are also hooks with double curves in three ways:
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are also hooks with three curves; and there are also hooks with one curve only, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these tools are sharp, and some only cut on one side, which is used to scrape the teeth, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these probes are bent in many ways, so that the patient does not hurt themselves when opening abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	They come in three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And they are only used in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and fingers, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to slices of fistula, according to this form, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes they put it into the place that heals by the opening of veins and arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men become swollen when they become corrupt, so that they resemble women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and if one wishes to cure them, one should bleed according to this form from this line b. up to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scorch the fat, and employ the wound with medicine that is charred, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing them, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags down, and is softened due to its size, as happens to women, then make two slits above them, by two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it eats away the remaining flesh and fat; then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the scalp
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the scalp are types of hard scrofula, and there are some that contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been expelled, fill it with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, they should be treated as we have described for fissures of scrofula; and if a wound opens in the abscess, they should administer cautery as we have described above.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is open and the skin above it is sealed, then abscesses often form there, and likewise it happens in swollen veins and abscesses.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows it thus when it is from the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a pulling; and when it is from the vein, there is a blue discoloration appearing;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpit and in the groin, and in the neck and many other places, and it is very serious.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	One should therefore avoid the use of cauterization with fire, and one should also avoid it in the case of a swelling on the skin caused by a rupture of an artery underneath.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then operate with a sharp knife, and carefully cut open the artery beneath the skin until it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle under the artery and pierce it all the way through to the other side, and compress the artery with a double thread in .ij. places, according to what I have instructed you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then tie off the area between the two ties with an intramuscular injection, allowing the blood to flow out and the abscess to drain;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that changes color, until the ligature breaks.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with ointment suitable for this, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to an opening in the vein, then you must dye your hand with something from the abscess all over the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then push the needle under the area you're holding in your hand and pierce it, and pass .I. double thread through it so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	bind the abscess, as I have told you, with a thread around both parts of the two joints;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you fear the thread will slip out, then tie another needle to one end of the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the thread in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then scrape the abscess until the excess comes out, then scrape away the excess from the skin and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a moistened cloth in wine and oil, then administer poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as an abscess comes in the artery and vein, there are abscesses of the nerves when they are hurt, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is a kind of neuralgia, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it has various dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when one presses it strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the surface of the body but deep inside;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and is mute in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor below or above, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: by chance they would contract;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or forehead, make the skin at the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, they cut it at the joint, then scrape off the skin, then remove the bone and close the wound with a stitch, and let it heal.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and is called "fungus" by some due to its appearance resembling oats, with thin roots and thick scabs; there are both small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two on his belly which looked more like fungi than anything else, without any other difference; they were white and had thin roots, and were split open, from which clear fluid was seeping.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found that one weighed 16 ounces and the other 20 ounces; the treatment for this is to ensure that the wound is moist, and the skin around it white and moist with thin roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the ulcer is large and deep, and there are cauteries at hand, for when cutting occurs too great a flow of blood, and if the blood drains away, then hasten to cauterize it.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with the knife, then take a good piece of white thread, and tie it around the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then release it, and do not stop tightening the thread around the joint until it is healed; and if the roots are large, then fear of piercing applies equally to the abdomen, but you can certainly pierce half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to pierce the thin, discolored skin with poor sensation and a milky discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess with an ulcer, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery on an ulcer or a fissure in the skin, and it is on the belly or some other body part, as happens with other wounds, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries, depending on what came before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is due to an ulcer and the discharge from the boil, then the colour of the abscess should be similar to the colour of the body, and there should be easy movement without pain, and there should be multiple discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more varied; when pressed with the hands, it springs back, and then returns, and sometimes it is constricted, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and from great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue; it opens easily when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then abscesses open with these signs: large and hard, and they are punctured according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to wind, then there is swelling at the touch, and the work involves checking whether the appearance is due to arterial blood or venous blood, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If you need to leave the wound open, because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is in the intestine or the bowels, then you must instruct the patient to hold his breath and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the abdomen;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the area that you signed all over the abdomen,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then press down on the apex of the abscess to the bottom with a sharp instrument;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	bind it tightly with a strong thread or a firm silk cord, and let the nose be free;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then cut open half of the abscess over the ligature, and push your index finger in, and feel for the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the ligature, then free it and push the intestine back into the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find pus, take it out with a spoon, and scoop out the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery makes you go in the opposite direction, or the vein, then walk around well, then return to your work and take 2 needles, and thread 2 strong threads through them, and insert the needles into what you have made as a cross, so that you make a piercing;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then push the abscess out in 4 places over the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the hole as it is, and let the dead flesh come out on its own;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can cut it when it is subtle and oozing, then treat the wound as necessary, and lances the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as appropriate, and close the hole.
dou chancre	of cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the appearance of cancer, and how to treat it with medicine, and how to avoid using iron in its treatment; and we speak of cancers that develop in ulcers, and great care must be taken in their treatment. The ancients say that when a cancer is in a place where it can be easily reached, like those on the breast, or thigh, or similar places, then one must remove it entirely as soon as possible. But for large and old cancers, one should not attempt to treat them, because I have never known anyone to be cured of such; nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment for cancers that can be reached, as we have said, is to first purge the patient with black colewort, then let him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, and then treat the cancer itself. Then cut away all the hair around it, and remove the bone underneath without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow out freely, and squeeze the area with your hand or something else to ensure that all the blood is gone. If bleeding from an artery or vein makes the incision difficult, cauterize it until the blood vessels are sealed off. Then treat the wound further until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsyThe following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already described in the division the appearances of dropsy, and how the accumulation of fluid is caused, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment by medicine, and that which is cured by iron. There are only two appearances; these are tympany and hydrops, for they are deadly conditions. Therefore, when you treat this appearance of dropsy called "tympany" with medicines, and the cure does not help, consider whether the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as dysentery and similar ailments; in that case, do not use iron, for there is doubt. But if you see the patient is very strong and has only dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then you must proceed thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Take the patient's hand and press his abdomen to force the fluid to the lowest part of the penis. Then take the spathumile (a medical instrument) with thorns according to this form: It should be a quarter-inch wide at the tip, but not so sharp that it can pierce all the way to the intestine when inserted, nor so blunt that it cannot penetrate;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then check if the dropsy is caused by the intestines: in that case, you must split under the skin on the right side of the penis three times. If it is caused by the liver disease, then the split should be on the left side; and if it is caused by the kidney, then it should be on the right. The patient should not lie on the split so that the excess fluid does not flow to that weak spot;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	perce the entire skin with the instrument and then pierce through to the spatumile, leaving your hand on all of it between the skin and the syphac as when scraping off a hangnail or around the nail; then pierce the syphac until the spatumile comes to the desired place, which is where the water is, and then pull out this instrument from which the shape is taken: It resembles a thin silver needle, and it is made of copper or light bronze, with a small hole in its base; on one side there are three holes, on another two, on another one, and the head is shaped like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes use to shape their pens:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the top is the funnel, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it then falls back onto the instrument; therefore empty half or a third, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the shock of the weapon to his spirit, or he will fall unconscious, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of his strength and according to what the dispositions of his strength indicate, and his pulse; then pull out the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the skin that blocks the hole that I mentioned above, which you pierce in this manner; then return to the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw off a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	make this on any day, and keep from drinking until there is only a little water left in it. And if you doubt the disease, leave it with a lot of water, then cure the grave or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and by drinking; and cure with medicines that dry up after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without a foreskin, or with a small foreskin, or it is not in its proper place. So one should immediately pierce it with a very fine needle according to this form: then put into the foreskin a very fine piece of lead, and tie it and leave it for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the lead, and let him urinate, and then replace the lead; and perhaps none of this is needed, because the urine that comes out will not allow it to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those with a small foreskin, if treated with the lead cloth as we have said, will be enlarged. Those who do not have the foreskin in its proper place are impaired, because some are born with the foreskin at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the glans, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then the head of the penis and the glans are pulled out to the size of a feather, so that the foreskin tears in the middle, as it should be; and you must guard against bleeding which often occurs, and if it does, stop the blood with something that stops blood, and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come on the penis, and it is an ugly-looking wart; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must grasp them with a pair of fine tweezers, and pull off both the head and root completely, then moisten cotton with Egyptian ointment and apply it; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blister is malignant, of putrid color and stinking, then you must apply cautery to it. When you have pulled it off, and if the blister is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the blister that is inside; and when it is healed, cure the outside. For if you cure them both together, the skin of the penis will not be secure from being pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into his penis and scrotum; so you must cut away all that is black and rotten, then apply an ointment of honey and wheat flour made from pomegranate peel and poppies, then cure it with other cures until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if there is bleeding, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cautery has two purposes: for bleeding and for corruption. And if the glans of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must tie a string around the shaft of the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin at the tip of the penis is torn, as happens to those who have not been circumcised, or due to a wound or an abscess, then you must cut away the foreskin with a sharp instrument, so that the ligature is released and the glans of the penis is freed all around.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a serious matter to discuss this, then you must cut away the foreskin with a sharp instrument from the tip of the penis and the skin; then untie quickly between two, and place a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water over it so that it does not tear again.
de la circoncision	on circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a natural process like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this act intentionally, especially on children, it is necessary to do it properly and gently for their safety.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing on this subject except what we have acquired through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and surgeons who made circumcision all around the foreskin, and in many places, and on every new-born; then the hyleus would coagulate because there are two membranes, and sometimes one above would coagulate and the other below would remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they cover it again and the pain is doubled; and in the cleaning of the foreskin, which is not completely healed at the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the fingernail, sometimes the nail escapes the fire, and the wound runs, and many times they are born with no need for cleaning, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning made on the foreskin there is always the danger of cutting too much from above and below. I have found through experience that this is the case with all cuts.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, you cut it evenly all around; but the thread should be well tied around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the rod, and then you make him stretch in every way that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then hold the rod between your hands straight, and press the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, or any of the instruments; then insert your hand into the rod and breathe on the skin, and pull it upwards until the head of the rod is in; then cleanse it well of the dirt that has accumulated there, then tie the site with a double thread, then tie it under one pouch to another string; and hold it with both hands by the second binding to the bag and the index finger, and pinch between the two strings, then release the skin quickly and pull the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the wound; and put powder on top of the powder a cloth glued with an egg yolk cooked in rose water, confit with good and fresh rosemary oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tense and pointed, and the heads should be as large as the palm equally:
