li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of purification occurs when the pus inside is exposed to the incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your fingernail, so that the skin forms an abscess; and then cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, hold it with tweezers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for 3 days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, let it be until the abscesses are reduced and the skin is lightly scraped; then cut as you can, taking care not to harm the foreskin in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the site of the wound with a powder, as we have described in the treatise on powders, and if it cuts too deeply into the skin, and it bleeds, it will not hurt; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.Et s’il advenist que li leus se deschause et ne puet apaiser, si doit on la couper legierement, si com il est dit au traitier de l’escorche, et si le leu est sanez, si ne nuira point; car il advenit maintes fois que li leus se deschaussent, et se l’on ne le cope, il advenist que la verge se chaude et se fende, et il advenist que li leus se dessuche de la verge.
dou retenement de l’urine	holding back urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stones, or frozen blood, or a tumor, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained by the stone which is lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be made to stoop on his knees, and have his feet placed on his back, and press his belly from above the back, and restrain himself as hard as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is forced upwards by compression, causing the stone to be expelled and the urine released;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and then you collect the urine that comes from the bladder into a clean vessel; and if it does not flow as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use an instrument called a «syringe», which has this form: it should be made of thin, lightweight silver, like the quill of a bird; the tube should be about a palm and a half in length, with a fine point at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	The method for releasing the urine is as follows: take a double thread, and tie a small ball of wool or cotton at the end, and insert the threaded end into the syringe; then dip the excess wool into the syringe, and grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a chair, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then lightly insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the scrotum; then fill the syringe up to the bladder, and the patient will feel the pain reach the empty space; this is not done according to this order unless the guide where it goes is wrong; then tie the thread to all the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	then restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are cuts or bleeding in the bladder, or when pus is accumulated, and you see the fluids and medications dripping, then do all the instruments that are called "clepsydra", and this is how it is formed:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see. The medicine used to stop the flow should be such that it blocks the penis without any addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and push when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see your medicine flowing into the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture and draw it out with the string that is inside. Then pull the string firmly towards you, and the moisture will enter the catheter and go into the bladder, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is how the subtle catheter works to treat the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or bronze, and the head is higher up; below, there are two strings attached to it. Then take a lamb's bladder and put in it the moisture that you want to use to catheterize the bladder. Then tie the two strings formed from a long double thread together, and heat one end of the moisture over the fire. Then insert the tip of the catheter into the penis, and then pull your hand towards the bladder gently, so that all the moisture goes in, and the patient will feel it when it reaches the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle out of it, and pierce it all around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as you would assemble a bag, and put inside whatever you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, squeeze it with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have described the difference between a stone lodged in the ureter, and all the signs, and in which kind of stone one should operate with cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will now tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs more often in children, and it is a sign that the urine flows from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it causes pain in the penis, and the patient may urinate many times, and then the flow stops; and many of these have the hernia; and the cure is much easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is appropriate first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces which is in the intestines. For it sometimes obstructs the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and make him stand up and move around so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out from above; then let him sit between your hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then feel it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten to cut above the stone. And if it does not come out with touching from below, then wet your index finger of the left hand with oil, if the patient is adult, or with middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put him into his anus, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, push it toward the neck of the bladder; then press above on your finger, and put it out where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command the patient to extend his testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand pull back the skin beneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatulum, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And they make it between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel; and it should be straight on the stone, and both hands should be on the anus, and the incision should go through the navel so that it is wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Perhaps the pressure from the hands on the anus will cause it to come out without much effort; and you should know that there is stone which has angles and edges: this is hard to pass; and there is also one which is beneath, similar to a grape, and round, whose passage is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you should grip it with forceps which are like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert a thin instrument beneath, and if the blood vessels burst, you stop the bleeding with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there is more than one stone, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then push up, then pull it out, and the smaller ones after, if there are several. And if it is very large, split it, and make a larger incision. For there are two things that can happen to the patient: they may die, or the urine will come out where the urethra cannot heal; but in any case, try to extract it, either by pulling with forceps, or by breaking it into pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have finished your work, smear the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and place over it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water to soothe the hot abscess; then remove the bandage from the patient's neck after three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, wash the area well with oil and water, then treat the wound with ointment of diaphenicon and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses and scorchings, and congealing of blood in the bladder, occur due to this, and urine is retained, which is known in such a way that it passes out with the urine: therefore, pierce your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and burst it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and aid him in every way you know how, until it is healed; and you ought to every hour that you treat him, bind his thighs together, and apply the remedies to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the penis, and lodged there, and the urine cannot pass; then the cure of what I have said before, that you should cut it many times, is an excuse for not cutting with this cure. I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form, and let it be pointed at three angles, and fix it into a stick:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the iron into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron in your hand within the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then the urine will come at once, then press your hand on what is left of the stone which is inside the penis. Then it is broken at once, and comes out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the penis in between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood from the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes stones become stuck in women, and if they do, the cure is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who can be examined by midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	The third reason is that one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of medicine; and the fourth is that the stone in a woman is often deeper than in a man, so a deeper incision is required, and great fear is associated with it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you find it necessary, you should consult a skilled midwife, and with her guidance, cut it out; and if you cannot find such a midwife, then consult a wise old woman or a woman who knows something about medicine. Have her examine the patient to determine the location of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then she must push her finger into her vagina and feel for the stone; and if she finds it, she should hold it under her finger, and she should be instructed to push her finger into her vagina with the pain, and press her left hand hard against her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then she must move the stone slowly from the entrance of the bladder up to the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the vagina where it is moving, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her finger over or under the stone, and let the incision be small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone so that you can widen the incision enough for the stone to come out; and know that there are many types of stones: some are small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and have various shapes. So know their likenesses in order to know how they will come out.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood is flowing, put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task, until the stone is out, and have some instruments that I told you about in extracting stones from men to help you with your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood flows, and it is from an artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the spot and bind it tightly with bandages, and do not loosen it again, but leave the stone and do not remove it, for otherwise the patient may die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wound has healed, return to your work until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous pus is nothing else but an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is located beneath the heart of the testicles and contains the sperm; and it is called "pus", and sometimes it is found within the membrane of the testicle, as if it were another testicle; and what we have said is the skin of the testicle between the white pus. And this does not usually happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this disease is from weakness which comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread about.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colours; it is sometimes jaundiced-coloured, or red, or black, or watery white, and more besides.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this condition, for if it is in the white scrotum which we have described, then there are swollen testicles, i.e., they are slightly long like the shape of an egg, and do not open the scrotum, because there is moisture all around them.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the scrotum itself, then there are swollen testicles with part of an egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white scrotum, he feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe throughout the entire area of the foreskin, from which the shape is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, what comes after the foreskin, judge what is inside it.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be healed according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then he should lie on his back, on something slightly raised, and have a lot of coverings under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side and instruct the attendant to sit on his right, and extend the foreskin to one of the two testicles near the heart;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatulum and cut the skin of the testicles from above down to the scrotum, and make the incision straight, cutting through the skin of the testicles to the white skin underneath, and then carefully peel it away.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the testicle with a large needle and draw out all the water, then insert your probes, and the testicle will go back up. Do not touch the skin of the testicles, but only the scrotum; cut it all around carefully, in sections if necessary, so that you do not cut too deeply and make it bleed, for otherwise the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the testicle has fallen out of its socket during the operation, then reset it in its place when you have finished with the scrotum. Then sew up the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a single stitch and dress the wound as you would any other, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by some other disease, then you must tie off the vessels that are suspended, fearing an effusion of blood; then cut the testicle away at its very suspension, and extract it, and dress the wound as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if pus is collected in two parts together, know that they are two pockets; then press the other part just as you did the first equally, then wash off the blood, and put into the wound soft lamb's wool moistened with rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another piece of lamb's wool moistened with wine and oil, and place over the two pockets, and put over it doubled cloths, and bind it all over to follow this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with lamb's wool according to this shape and have them sewn together at the crotch of the breeches, and let one of the heads press against the bottom up to the back, and the other to the part of the armpit; and let the other two heads be over the two angles, and let all the binding be in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this pocket is medicated with an iron brand, and it is that you press a thin knife cautery, and press the skin of the pockets, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the fluid is exposed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the wart deeply, and scorch it with this fine hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cup in every way you can, until you draw it all out; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and move while guarding against bloodletting, and movements of the knife.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything makes you contrary, either a warm abscess or bloodletting or anything else, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horrible nature, then administer piercing, as I have told you, and it is certain that when you are well through the indications we have discussed,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	let the patient sit on a high chair; then pierce the abscess at its base to the full length of the spatula, and insert the piercing deep into the body; and let the holes be large enough for all the pus to flow out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the site and bind it, and let it drain to remove the remaining pus; then treat the wound until it is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white film does not let the pus out through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a syringe or the instrument used to treat dropics, of which the shape is described earlier; and widen the wound slightly, and know that the pus will return, and it will accumulate again after six months or around that time, and when it accumulates as before, and thus the patient will recover.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the dissection of this nerve there are several dispositions which cause fear, so it seems better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you about the procedure and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	So I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially in the groins; and this is due to various causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is known to be caused by excess bitterness and redness, which is spread throughout the body, or from a blow.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not hurt at all, and is a serious abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes there are green, fearful, and watery abscesses, and at other times they come from an artery, or from a vein swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	Those who are affected by swelling of the veins are recognized by their appearance and the touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well judge the extent of this condition, and other similar ones,

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles

de la routure dou syfac	of the rutting of the syphilis
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The cause of this disease is through the incision that comes from syphilis, or the swelling on the belly in the region of the intestines, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture to one of the testicles;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is from syphilis, or from the swelling of it, and these two ways come from causes: from percussion, or jumping, or crying out, or lifting a heavy object, and through similar things;

Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white ulcer we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and it leaves the wound open until it drains through it; and if it is slow to drain, one should use hot water, and apply what we have said, until it drains.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then treat the wound with another treatment until it is perfectly healed.Quant il y a grans vives douleurs sus li membre, si covient le membraier tant qu’il soit sanz dolor; et s’il est sanz dolor par lui mesmes, si est bien, car il n’a grant besoin de membraier.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch of medicine, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients say that it is done in the same way as the vein that is next to the artery, by tightly binding them together after making an incision just above the testicles.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut it open halfway, and treat the abscess of the one who has it, until the vessels drain; and cure it as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the intestines, as we have said, and it opens up; and none of the intestines fall out into the rectum, and if any do fall out, it is only a little bit, and they return at every movement.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And even if he stays too long in that position, the patient believes that the wound or fistula will close up as long as the intestines do not fall out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens because of the extension of the fistula in the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended and then softened and swollen and opens up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the treatment if by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and let the patient lie face down on his back between your hands, then press hard on the wound with your fingers according to the amount of .iii. times;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	then pull out the sty that is underneath the skin, then take the thread and place it over the visible area of the sty;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	then press down on the bottom of the belly, then tie off the two visible areas of the sty on the head of the thread, and tie one and then the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull out the head of the thread, and do not touch the sty or stretch the skin or anything else, just as I have told you in the cure for a rupture of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat with the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilis is restrained, and has no appearance in the buttock, and the cautery is more effective in this area, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles becomes soft in some men because the parts inside become soft, and it is milky in appearance; and when one wishes to treat it, one should make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the scrotum; then sew together the two edges of the wound with a single stitch, or two stitches or four, firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the sutures.
dou chastrement	chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Do you know that castration is considered taboo in our laws, and because of this, I would prefer not to discuss it in this book; it is only necessary for two reasons: one, so that the doctors can respond when asked about it, and know how to perform the procedure; and two, because we often need to castrate certain animals to aid us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts. Therefore, I say that castration is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision. When done by attraction, one sits the animal in warm water until its testicles are softened and dangling; then, squeeze them with your hand until they are removed and you no longer feel anything. For the castration by incision: tie the animal down, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand; then cut above the scrotum, and cup over each testicle a dozen times, when you have cut them well; and leave some pus and the fine membrane covering the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the one by attraction, because in the latter, sometimes something remains from the testicles, causing the animal to desire sexual intercourse; then cure the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites exist in two ways as males: one type has both male and female characteristics, with the physical appearance of a male, including body hair, but sometimes their urine flows upwards. The other type is found in females, who have a penis and testicles on their groin. For both types, if they have an opening between the testicles, treat them as you would any other wound; cure them like any other wound. But for the second type, where the male's urine flows out through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	of the testicles
de erratique	of erratica
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratica is when the woman's nature is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that came to it; or it is due to a growth, or a subtle and thick syphilis, and it is caused by an ulcer in the wound, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and they affect conception and childbirth, and perhaps flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is through the examination of the bail. If the stump is clearly apparent, then seek it with your fingers or a string. If it is a subtle syphilis, and it is close to the testicles, then you must hasten and pull them thus: place your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back with her legs spread; then the testicles will become erect, so that the subtle syphilis is drawn out, and cover the stump; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman lie down at home every day so that it does not adhere. And if the syphilis is hard and thick, you should cut it with spathumile similar to bay leaf. If the stump is of a newborn character, then it should be covered according to this manner, if it is not encrusted abscesses. For in the abscess encrusted in the wound, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroides are openings of veins from which blood flows excessively, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into throbbers; and I have already described their appearances, signs, and treatments in the previous section. I stated that both hemorrhoids and throbbers, when they are deeply rooted in the anus and do not respond to natural remedies, can be cured with iron instruments. For those located at the entrance of the anus, one can feel them and treat them effectively. Therefore, one should place the patient in a cool room, cut off the hemorrhoids with tweezers, and apply powder made from blood-restraining medicines like acacia, dragon's blood, and incense to the roots of the hemorrhoids. Then, one should bind her feet against the wall for an hour and immerse her in cold water. If bleeding occurs, one should make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, gallnuts, and similar ingredients. Next, prepare a poultice of barley flour mixed with honey and garlic, and apply it to her back. If there is no discharge, one should use leeches on her back and breasts without using iron instruments. Then, take lamb's wool, soak it in plantain juice or dogwood juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the affected area. Once the abscess has drained, treat the wound with ointment until it heals completely. The type called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough surface; it should be treated like a throbber as mentioned earlier and then healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of anal abscesses
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that can occur in the anus, such as chancres, pierous abscesses, herpes, estiomata, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, among others, which I have described in the previous section. Now, I will discuss the treatment of hot abscesses that arise in the anus and are not caused by bowel movements. If you notice that the abscess is hard, accompanied by fever and a red color at the beginning of its onset, do not rush to pierce it immediately. Instead, wait until the pain subsides, and then have the patient sit on a low seat with two small pillows to lean against for support. The patient should also bend their legs and spread their buttocks, placing their arms under their knees, and tie them with a strong cord. Then, suck the orifice of the abscess towards the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the anus, being careful not to go too deep and cause discomfort or bleeding. If the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the anus with cloth so that it does not cause any distress. Insert the tip of the instrument and then withdraw it, allowing the content to flow out. Then, clean the wound with soft tenters soaked in rose oil or linseed oil, placing the tender against the wall of the wound at the deepest part of the anus. Place another piece of linen soaked in warm water or a decoction of malva flowers and aristolochia over the anus and around the wound, and change it every two days until it is healed. If there is pus discharged from the wound, apply a poultice made from crushed beans and honey to the affected area. Once the wound has drained, treat it with appropriate ointments as mentioned earlier. If there is no discharge, one can also use enemas of warm water mixed with honey to clean the wound and promote healing.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the natural signs of childbirth, and to understand that when you see a woman straining and pushing downward, and desiring to smell aromatics; then the child will soon be born. You should also observe the signs that the birth is natural, such as the child emerging head-first, with the placenta following close behind. The mother's excess fluids are expelled through good cleansing. Any other position of the child indicates an abnormality in the process. It may come out feet-first, or through the chest, arms, abdomen, or back; it might even get stuck on its neck. The midwife must be wise and shrewd in these matters, guarding against mistakes and deception. I will now describe all the positions of the child, explaining how to assist in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child emerges head-first in a natural delivery, but the woman is struggling and weak, then seat her on a stool or have other women support her. Boil an ointment of olive oil or fenugreek, and use a small spatula (as described below) to gently open the child's mouth:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If the two hands emerge, gently pull them back in one by one. If they cannot be pulled back, then seat the woman on a chair with her feet raised; then lift the chair off the ground and tilt it forward so that she is leaning backwards. If the hands still cannot enter, use the technique described earlier to dislocate the child's neck and pull out the arms.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the child's feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child is born feet first, he should be turned upside down;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn him slowly, until he is straight;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then hold one of his feet and stretch it out slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just up to its hips, instruct it to grab and make it sneeze from the back;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't jump as we have said, then turn it gradually, as long as it is according to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take musk, and oil of sweet almond, and molten gum, and grind them all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply this ointment according to the nature of the woman
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then let her sit in warm water up to her ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is soaked underneath, make a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently squeeze her abdomen, for the child will now jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child emerging onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife should put her hands on him little by little.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then let it be laid on its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bends his hands little by little, then presses his hands on the belly, and lifts the cushions underneath, until she is ready to go down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the baby doesn't come out, grab her feet and move them around, then move your hand on the belly upwards, then put in your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and pull the child out little by little; and instruct the woman to hold on until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes from a wide one hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	You should try to bring the hand back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if you can't bring it back, then have the woman stand up and walk. If that doesn't work, then:
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she can't walk, then have her lie down on a bed and raise her legs straight up;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the medicine that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on a chair, then study to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's exit from his neck, and has his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I must have him hold his hand, then turn it slowly little by little, and gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then apply to it a poultice of mustard and oil, as we have said, then instruct the patient to move it little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a chair, and instruct her to sneeze; and make her yawn.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way with all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way throughout the afterbirth, then catch the afterbirth with your fingernail, as long as the moisture is expelled;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can press its face and neck with its fists, and the mother does not restrain it, then the child will die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the baby inside, as you should, and instruct the woman to hold on tight sometimes:
adonques si istra legierement.	then let go gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's birth
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes there are three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	But two is a strange thing, and they do not live, if at all.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiple, and are separated by the placenta that divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue as naturally as one, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are bleeding heavily, then apply the cautery as we have said, and be nimble and quick in what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is best for her health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb: one, two, three, four, five, six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious Sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to know all of this, because similar things might happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if they act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating a woman of a dead child or in labor, as I have said in the previous chapter, and there is no progress, and you are forced to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if you need to know whether the woman is of sound health and has no fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	the woman should be laid on her back, with her hips tilted down and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife should apply a compress of ten parts to the womb, keeping her in bed so that she is not distressed by the child's descent.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mother's mouth with moist oils infused with mugwort and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint her palms with these oils and infusions.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then he lightly strikes them, then he seeks out the joints where they are convenient for this,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and takes care that the child is positioned so that it descends onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he inserts them into his eyes or throat or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, he should push or pinch and press on the middle of the shins;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the needle in his right hand and places the thread between the fingers of his left hand, and wraps it around all of his hand lightly, and inserts the needle into one of the locations we have mentioned so that it reaches the hollow;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the needle:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce with another needle, or a third one if you need it, so that the extraction is equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then they are moved equally from one side to another so that they exit, and the needles are bitten to hold them in place, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then anoint some of his fingers with oil, and put them in that part, and draw out the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if nothing remains, then place this joint higher or lower, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back due to the dislocation,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must wrap him in a cloth, as much as he can go;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cut at the joint of the sole or the heel, and so you should do in the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the head of the child is large and it is congested at the exit, or there is acute swelling in the head,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	you should push the spine-like spatumile between your fingers, puncturing the head and drawing out the congestion;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and so naturally the fetus grows to a large head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pulls out the bones with tongs,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head pops out and is forced, so that the moisture which is in the wound issues forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot exit, then cut it into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, the pulse is light, and the healing is swift at the mouth of the wound.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or foot, then you must stretch it with .i. bandage wrapped around his hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and cut the belly or foot, so that the moisture which is in it runs out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are dislocated, and the shoulders remain,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	if he puts his hand in the wound deeply, and pulls it until it reaches the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he puts in .i or ii inches, and pulls it out;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has formed there, then one must not work on it,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then one must apply moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and poultices, and apply warm moistening and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can get it to lie still, then administer what we have said for a living child:
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot, then let the birth take place in parts, and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it is administered to those we have mentioned in abscesses that occur in the sea;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there is bleeding, let it be put in hot water restraining, and let other remedies be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some children had been dead, then another was sewn onto it, and the others died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her in the groin, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to emit a foul odor.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought long, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong attracting plaster, and an bone came out, and after a few days, some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	Examine the wound, and with your fingers, move the bones until the woman is in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and let the woman stay like this for a long time, and then move her slightly from side to side.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have included this chapter especially because when the masters encounter something unusual, they should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocated back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the press, to which one applies books; and at .2. turns for .2. chaps of .2. strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle of the constrictor, and should be made of box or of yew;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the stalk should be one digit wide, and the edges of the trees one digit, and in length a palm and a half;
