mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must inquire into the dislocation, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but be careful that the vein or nerve do not cause any harm;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knives and probes used to cut these bones are many, depending on the position of the bones and the appearance of the teeth,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason one must prepare for each kind of operation its appropriate instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to your knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and to testify to the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	then prepare the instrument that you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may dislocate due to an internal or external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with remedies, but they are of no benefit,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	you must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion is located,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient does not escape through death or through greater harm from the defective limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black and seems to be burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then comes darkness, after which this corrosion of members spreads member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and affects the whole body; so take care to cover it up quickly,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creature, such as a sea-scorpion, adder, or similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head or neck, then cover it and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, then the cautery at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then the cautery at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no amelioration for this beyond the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus it is done when the cautery comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then the cautery after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, it affects the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, it affects the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to cauterize the disease to death;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the method of cauterizing the member, whether with fire or with silk, is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one servant one of the lines downstream, and another servant the other line upstream,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dislodge the joint which is between the two lines to a width of one digit, as far as the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the wound or cut, and place from each side a piece of linen, so that the silk does not touch the healthy area,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring about another injury and abscess in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if you see blood flowing when you are working, then cauterize the spot firmly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the dislocated member with a suitable ligament, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in his sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	there happened to him a blackness which seemed like a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion began in his toe of the foot, so that it affected the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered the foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after, the corrosion returned to his finger on the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed upon it things that would cause reverberation after the purification of the body, but could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to touch his hand, and I refused because I had no hope that I would reverberate the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I was also afraid that if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's strength was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he covered his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other cure to tell of except for this one, if anyone has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and discharges, and the place remains hollow, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin on top is as delicate as a loose napkin.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach the bone or nerve; such an illness is called "healthy."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula."
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends to the bone, then it is called a  "fistula."
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and cook it until you cover the entire skin, especially when it is thin, just like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not add anything to it for flavor.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you see that the skin is burning and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine whether the breasts are large, and the navel which is in them has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse with an Egyptian medicine enema made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafätida, oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take some of this according to your need, and make it into water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it as a suppository in the breast, and constrict the opening;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for .ij. hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times until the breast is healed and the pore is closed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are cauterized with water from ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you should take ash wood from a vine and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it and use it to enema until you know that the bowels are clean.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, or the Egyptian medicine or the water from ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if you use an enema of water and honey or one with a little litharge powder ground up in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can enema with honey and melted wine, as honey has the property of purifying and washing out.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes it sweat.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this, and are confident that the intestines are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you enema with that which causes flatulence within him,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you press a suppository gently, and they make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you can enema with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the rectum is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	loosen it with a blade a little, and put in some Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, until it is loosened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then cut and leave only enough space for the catheter to enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the anus is above, then cut higher up or lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is at full stretch, one must not let the arrow fly.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the bow points to the lowest place it can reach,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is at full stretch, one must not let the arrow fly.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	prepare it in this way: let the bow run smoothly downward, and leave nothing of the bow behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place them on a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then press down firmly on the opening of the armpit . The second hole should be larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft ointment on another piece of cloth according to the size of the hole,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the armpit to ease the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth for several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And whoever is above the armpit, remove often to remove the bow,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what flows from the bowel, whether it is venom, or little, or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that rises above the opening of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breasts are soft, and approach health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change another bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows badly after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons spread after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because there are people who slowly heal their wounds with poultices, and those that do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if milk doesn't flow from the breast after many days, know that the breast won't produce milk.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to produce milk and are distant, then apply moist remedies in substance but dry in nature,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as with an ointment that is diaphanous, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and that is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take a definite ointment, and they make it with rose oil, and rose wine of equal substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then they cook it and use it; and with that same one makes honey cooked thickener,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when a definite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and the powder on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue a cloth to it, and apply pressure to the chest, and sometimes they administer an aromatic long poultice,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is as fine as wheat flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or compounds: grind them to a powder, and mix with the honey I have mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long, and is not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that the corruption is complete, and makes an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on soft tissues;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	as we have said before, if the treatment for a fistula.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that develops underneath the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from the foot, or perhaps it grows in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes infected, and no care is taken, then an abscess forms,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they grow and ooze pus until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps they grow all the way;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the toe becomes swollen, and its color is purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess tissue that has grown from under the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then you should cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is very helpful if both the bone and nail are healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to poke through, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you should put some thread under the nail so that it doesn't hurt the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pull upwards, and gently push down on the flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put burning and corrosive medicine on the rest of the flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with poultices until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decaying, pull it out with a pair of tongs as mentioned earlier,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must treat it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the big toe diagonally from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cutter does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	You should treat a tumor that grows in the hands of some people by chance, which is all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes it has bones and sometimes nails,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some grow at the root of the joints, where the growth is in some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a hernia in his navel should not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the navel, perhaps moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of one who is fleshy, if it is slight in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; if you hold it tightly, it will stop bleeding.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For one who is born in the anus, you must cut the flesh around the anus first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone to a convenient depth, then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from arson, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary to cut this wound so that the parts may join together according to their natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or wet cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of thin plaster, until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of his hands with the palm, then cut that wound as it should be.
Des vils	Of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large enveloped tubes filled with melancholy humors, which come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more frequently in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purgative, and then the basilicum herb.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with fire can be done in two ways: one is to apply it directly to the skin and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other way is to open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	Incision should be performed in the following manner: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg from the patient's thigh down to just below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open a vein in one place, or two or three places, of a broad size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then press and milk out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the nature of the illness can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then have him drink some red wine mixed with black gall;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume the bleeding and the bloodletting when the veins are full, and it is harmful to the illness.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The remedies for this are as follows: shave the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply the poultice to the vein from the top of the knee down to the ankle or just below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the vein's origin, and scorch the vein on each side until it bleeds when pressed;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pierce the vein underneath, so that it is raised from the skin, and then it can be bound tightly at the wrist,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut the skin above in three places; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then open it with a razor, as you did before, and bind it at another wrist, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another size, or several if you need them, then lift it, and cut it to the toe of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift it until the second size; then pull it out by size until it is all loose, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it, and insert it under the skin, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and ensure that it does not crack, because if it cracks, then one cannot milk or lift it, and this brings harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished milking it, place a pad soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the head is bent, twisted, and wrapped together, not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you should split it crookedly, but do not crack it; and milk it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut unless it touches the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes they grow elsewhere than on the legs, and this happens with warts that come underneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like snakes and worms which creep between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes color, and the vein starts to protrude outward, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, you must wrap it around with a piece of woolen cloth from one and a half inches to two and a half inches, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth hang down to the leg, and every time it comes out of place, wrap it around the cloth again, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap around the remainder, and do not cover it at all in its root, until it has come out entirely;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and swelling in that spot, and a serious illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this reason it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing should remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is treated from five to ten inches long,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man came to me whose vein was cut from ten inches long, and when you cover it, it forms a lump or hole, and pierces all the way to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and after emptying the matter inside, bring healing medicines to it for several days, then heal it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein bleeds more when it opens at the joint of the foot, or the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there is much bleeding and it spurts; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms which grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of oxen" because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm which grows between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body both upward and downward,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it travels from limb to limb, as far as it can go under the skin, then it breaks out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by the putrefaction of some humours, like worms and snakes and roundworms and hookworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him bleeding and milking, he cannot hold back until he has finished:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top of it and bleed him forcefully; if the pus is deep in his flesh and you do not release it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize with fire on top, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then press firmly under the eyelid, then pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one must use the patient's body with purifying medicines for dissolved evil humours;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there is pus coming from wounds caused by burning meat.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain which comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our language, and it is a pain that occurs in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and can move from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling on the vein in her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up as high as a worm at her shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, as if it were bright silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that spot and moved to her shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran throughout the body until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she began turning around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from limb to limb in this manner, for I had never seen this illness act in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had felt pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have not seen this in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and due to this constraint, the wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and rested veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it reveals itself as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	examine it above and below thoroughly, and then press upon it until the windiness constrained in the place comes out;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	let the one who dislodges windiness, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar ones.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearance and according to where they land on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is that there are those which have large points, small points, hooked points, and blunt points.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And there are differences in arrows according to the heart that carries them: for there are some from a strong heart and some from a fearful heart; and you must know how you should guard yourself in all ways, as I will teach you. And there are those with two angles, those with tongues, and those with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which occurs in any limb, it occurs according to two ways: or in a principal limb it dislocates,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lung, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore occurs in any of these members, and the signs of death which I will tell you about below appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be careful about the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully out, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps out the sphenoid sinus which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there are cuts and wounds and bleeding, and inflammation and redness of the eyes, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and it may also be that there is blood coming out of the nose or ears; and it may cause loss of speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is white moisture coming from the wound, resembling pus, and also coming out like blood from a wound.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, stop the bleeding, and remove the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were pierced into a hard object, not hollow;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the wound becomes mute like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the lung is that there is no pain from foam coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the cover of the foot, it is between the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great discomfort and breathing difficulties; and all the limbs from the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance some indigestible meat may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the chest or belly, and no feces come out through the intestines, then there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, spine of the back, hip, thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you how to do this.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	To .I. man an arrow fell into his shoulder at the root of the nerve:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and dislodged it from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I dislodged an arrow that had lodged in the fat of the eyelid below the eyeball,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was pushed back so that only the tip was visible above the surface,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and was struck by a large arrow from a Turkish bow, right through the ear; the wound healed, and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he received an arrow in the throat from a Christian, and the arrow was an Arab one, going through the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs and extracted it gently, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he received an arrow in the stomach from a man, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person who has an arrow shot into his back, and the wound is closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions do not change,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	he found no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow shot into his face and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I saw an arrow shot at a man of the king's party, who was hit in the eye,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was all drawn out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the sickbed after she had been sick for three days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her with a small needle and didn't feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and felt numbness and pain below her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed on the wound a digestive and astringent plaster, to prevent inflammation of the eye;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the eye of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster more often, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow one day within his flesh; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was healed
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed the wound and felt the head of the arrow which was lodged there;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied the corrosive medicine to the wound again and again until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and transgresses the terms for about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then lacerate the wound that I pricked with tweezers, and tore at from both sides, but could not extract it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not cease to use subtlety and cunning with instruments until one day I took it with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to how it was described in this chapter, so that I treated it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I therefore restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I will tell you about the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may focus on what I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters consider well a little great thing, and what is present and lacking to them;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they seek new work, and new tools, and the descending of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the limbs where they are stuck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumped out of there where it entered, is an arrow entering their flesh, and sometimes jumps out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, then leave it until the wound around it has healed over, and the opening has closed up.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for a few days, moving it slightly each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if not, then pierce around it with a very thin needle, until the area around the wound is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and penetrates to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient; then do not extract it, but let it be until it becomes even and smooth after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow penetrates to the sinus, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone at all, and does not penetrate to the sinus,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, if the method of extraction is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deep and cannot come out, then administer cauterizations around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body and cannot be seen, then it must be sought out throughout the entire body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then extract it with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut as deeply as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrowhead that are holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut the flesh that is stuck to the arrow's barbs as deeply as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then breaks or folds the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, which you will pull more violently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot in one go, then leave it until around the joint is swollen; then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes you feel faint, then administer what we have said about curing in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and opening a vein, and use whatever means you can to pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and treat the patient according to how they were when the arrow struck them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the best help you can give them; and if you cannot, then treat them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another direction, or where something can be seen or felt escaping from them, or where the skin is swollen:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut it off, therefore, as far as the pincers can reach, and then pull it out; if it does not come away at once, cut it again.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, then rotate your hand swiftly as far as it will go into the bone and widen the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then let it be for now and start the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a arrow in it, remove the entire arrow;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it is cut, and you see to administer a bandage, then let him administer .i. chewed instrument,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the gum of the instrument; and then bind it tightly,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is chewed, let him apply  .i  instrument with an entering point, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, then you must cut all around the flesh where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces in the thigh, or buttock, or belly, or bladder, or ribs, and it is deep, and you can reach it, then cut over it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then extract the arrow, and then stitch the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrow wounds resembles an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the tip that grabs the arrowhead is also like an owl's beak,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as shown in this drawing:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tongs for gripping and probing is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one heals, there are 31, and of these, there are 16 in the head,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: 2 veins that are behind the ears, which are called the two "ear-veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are visible in the two temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the eyelids of the eyes, called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is in the head of the neck;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the throat;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth; these are the veins called "eye-veins".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and 2 veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which we commonly bleed are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side, and people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the method is called "binding", and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it a "blood vessel"; and the basilic vein is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and common people call it a " belly vein ", and it is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one which opens clearly over the pubic area.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvatella is the vein between the little finger and ring finger, and also on both sides.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins; one is beneath the curve of the pouch on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second superficial vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called 'nesse', which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrh and by leeches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the healer, as I told you, and it is that you heal the head of the sick person,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the sick person's neck with a twist,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears, depending on the head in two places:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Take them to your fingers, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, press firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancelet, and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And pierce the skin and the vein well .ii. times, and let the blood flow until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries in the temples, if it is an old wound,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and eye-sores and blind eyes; and in the body of tears and ulcers;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the nature of the bleeding is as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels pain under your armpit, and then sign inward;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lightly press the vein above your armpit with your index finger, and insert the lance underneath,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lightly press the vein above, and constrict it, as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	then ligature it tightly, and let it until it heals; and we have spoken of their bandaging and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the frontal vein is just as good for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its qualities are such that the patient turns their neck while twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "digging", which is made as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and push with your hand or another object, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loose the collar around the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healthy and sometimes work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable for the flames to be too small; and heal it crookedly, because the bone is close by, and accidentally break the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two eyes helps them, and also helps with tetter, and redness, and eye infections, and facial illnesses.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	The nature of their healing is such that the patient should twist their neck using a bandage, as mentioned before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then he should heal it, and the healing should go through the wound, from the tip of the flame to a little way above it, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, they might break; then draw out the blood, as much as you need to, and then tie it up with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein from the nose is useful for headache, and for dizziness, and for facial ailments,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that occur in the face, and especially when they are chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient tilts their neck to the left, then pinches their nose on the same side,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a long, thin flame and inserts it into the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well, and now the blood will begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it off for a night, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of the .ij. gundages helps with strangulation of the gullet, and at the beginning of measles, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and stomach aches;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the healing is such that the patient stretches his neck upwards from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein widely, then draw the blood tempered, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same to the other vein, then untie the ligature, and bind both veins gently,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	letting the patient bleed until morning so that the wound can heal.
De la sainie des leivres	Of bleeding from the lips:
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins of the lips helps with ulcers in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and gum pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turns the lip, and looks at two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and one can identify them because they are black, and because around them there are thin black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	so take hold of both of them, and if you do not know them and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then take hold of the thickest one on each side, and it is the same method for those above and below, and for those on the right or left, and for those on the upper or lower lip; then take hold of the thickest one on each side, and it is the same method for those that are above and below, because it is the same thing.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding from the head, and it is for tightening the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeding are such that the patient holds his hands out in front of the sun, and touches the tongue, and looks under each side to see a black vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed both, but do not go too deep, as there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck from which blood is commonly drawn are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either with a sharp steel needle as thick as a thumb or with an olivary needle as fine as a hair, and it is called «ane sil».
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and narrow according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the steel needle is very important, and it should be as thick as a thumb:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth on top and contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of an olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and sharp, and is used to lance delicate veins, where there is delicate yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basil vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to cleanse the wound thoroughly and to cauterize the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he punctures the artery, and bleeding ensues, then it must be staunched as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the vein should not be punctured, but cut short as though it were a thread.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open up clearly, then you must stretch it and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you can cut a vein from it, or you can open the vein in the arm: it will become apparent.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the cautery to the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the vein for bleeding, you must stretch out the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot, release the arm, and cauterize the vein with the flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and make sure you do not pierce an artery when you see the spot swell up, for that is an artery; avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, as often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm, and leave it be, and do not move it until the patient is healed. And have him remain fearful, and do not let him move it until he is better.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and it flows, and you have no medicine at hand, then press upon the artery to open it, for that is where the blood retreats, and staunch the flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of elderwood, split it in half, and take one of the halves and tie it on tightly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the blood is staunched, that is good; if not, then stop it as we have said with powders that stanch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stanching is not effective in many cases due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of a vein is helped if it draws blood from the head above and the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	This is because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce too deep and find the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and if it swells and the saint is troubled, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens in many places, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, you must heal the instrument with your breath; then protect the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they will make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Healing of the cephalic nerve helps to attract blood from the head and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it should be healed by pricking with an olive or myrtle twig, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest method, and not worry if it fails the first time, but try again.
