et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes inflames the area in some people if it fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done solely for the sake of healing, but also to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the incision should be made in one of the three veins: these are, the cephalic, the fasting, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours in the morning.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but whenever there is a need, at any hour and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a child before the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be bled, in any manner, they should first clear the intestines with a gentle enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained much feces so that the veins are not attracted by the harmful superfluities from the intestines to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor is he healed who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk, as long as that lasts, nor the hydroptic.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if they are to be healed after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and from exertion, staying up late, and fasting, and anything that weakens them, either through the weapon or through the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then skillfully modify the humors, if the sickness is gross, through meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter the bath, if nothing else helps, to draw out the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein of the foot around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard against that day of labor, and puncturing, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyful, and let the healer be above those whom one heals, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the ligature above it, because if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot move;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then he rubs the area with his hands, until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then he moistens the needle with the flame of a little oil, then puts his finger from his left hand on the vein under the site where he wants to bleed,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not break when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which flow like strings to the heart, and others that are filled with air.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one places them over the flame, they withdraw from the heat and cannot open the vein, and so it is with these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, so the surgeon must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then try again a little lower on the same spot, or above, if the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient despondent, let him have a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	by chance there will be abscesses; do not enter the bath, then resume bleeding if she wishes;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the vein is small, cut it short and you doubt that it will not release as much blood as you want, then pierce that vein itself directly with a needle;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and open it slightly so that the limb becomes swollen; because this happens many times when the vein is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the site swollen, do not change the bandage and apply a little linseed oil, for it eases the body's blood and in this place the linseed is crushed.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil in each bandage that you dress the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this also makes a triacle and bowels move, when one puts it on the site; thus subtly the blood escapes and is scattered when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not bled first, or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hasten, and place on the site a sponge moistened with water and salt that is lukewarm, and compress it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the blood issues from the vein, and if it remains in place for a few days with no sign of blackness or greeness, then it does him no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see any swelling, place on it some aloe or myrrh that has been softened in the juice of hellebore, monkshood, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of pus at the site of the basilic vein; therefore, place your hand on it, and if you feel the area soft to the touch upon compression with your hand, then that appearance is bad.Et si tu veis, met sus le leu esponge moillie et chaut, ou l’estraincture de la main, si ne tu veis aucune noiror ou verdor;
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to put anything on it of what we have said, for by chance it might enter an artery; but let him make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then heal it with another healing, until it is cured.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person blood according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that one makes him a larger wound, and the flames are wider;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to those who are weak, do the opposite, and one must bleed little and often, and one should bleed by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this bleeding method is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And if the body needs bleeding, one should give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if it is scorched, then bleed three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of a cold complexion, one should eat moist bread before bleeding in rosewater syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and good-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints from the bleeding, after the loss of much blood, then he should breathe in the fumes of vinegar and subtle-scented syrup,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have discussed in the chapter on syncope for opening a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm again and again, then when it is weakened by excessive bleeding, he should bleed a little bit at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And those who want to bleed their arms again after the first bleeding, and they have strong bodies, should bleed again after seven hours, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed elsewhere, it must bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is a lot of blood inside the body that has been heated and causes fever; so we must draw out a large quantity and widen the orifice so that it drips out in drops.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then you should know all the ways to bleed, and put your hand over his pulse when he is bleeding so that death does not come through the orifice,
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the arm being dislocated, and blood coming out a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press directly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, that he extends his arm forcefully, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be until it heals the second time; then you may apply the tip of the flame to the frozen blood at the hole,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place a little bit of salt dissolved in water on it and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If a vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it until the abscess has been drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If necessary, bleed a second time in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are bled in the area of the vein in the head because it is more complex.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to bleed is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the vein turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let them be bound tightly, so that the vein appears well, then heal now through the middle, not the wide or long [part].
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the hole should be wide, and healed near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot issue from it, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and heal near the neck, and not too close to the hole so that the blood cannot issue and cause death. And if it is in summer, then do not push the hand into hot water, for we put it there more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salve for healing the right hand is good for all illnesses of the liver, and this is how to make it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Soak the hand in hot water until the vein is swollen, as far as one can see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is crooked and you cut it from top to bottom, it will not hurt at all.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	But do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely stripped of flesh underneath,and
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in warm water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as needed, put oil and silk on the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the right side, and do everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	Bleeding from the vein in the throat is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as diseases of the eyes, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the arms, legs, and older limbs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the nature of his healing is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs the vein until it opens.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lies down on the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot, many veins go there.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then heal it in the widest vein, or at the ankle, which is better.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well by coping; and let the flames be ανέσυλη.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing fails the first time, then try again the second time higher up a little, because the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do likewise with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its cure lies in the pain of the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its cure are such that the patient should immerse himself in a bath and twist his ankle four times in a circular motion.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise it will not open; and if it does open, then treat it in every way you know how, by applying pressure and stretching.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is good to cup the vein, for the site is safe, and it is very effective in treating many people.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, then cut a vein on either the back or the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Let the blood flow until you see it, then untie the ligature, place cotton on top and press it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Bleeding with leeches.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and bleeding is done according to 2 methods: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this farting which is without pain is according to two manners: either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and farting which is done by striking and by drawing blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	one of which is all in the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on either side of the neck; and the windpipe under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glasses on the .2. shoulders; and the cupping glasses above the kidneys;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping glasses in the .2. arms; and the cupping glasses on the .2. legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cupping glasses at the  .2. ankles; and the ventilation does not draw blood, except from small veins that are scattered throughout the body,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it weakens one no more than bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it must not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity or habit it is necessary to bleed, then we bleeding every hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in the middle and at all times.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some who experience fullness and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who spit up a drop of blood in their mouths, have swollen tongues, and ooze blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is during the month, we command them to fast after 3 hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Bleeding from the nose helps with headaches ... that comes from the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in the place of the healing of the cephalic,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and those of a cold complexion should not use it, nor those with catarrh, for it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those with head colds.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal from it become oblate, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a little lower down due to the risk of oblateness.Car li veillart et cil qui ont chief froides maladies, si conviennent que les ventoses soient plus avals sur la cephalique, car ce lor fait grant bem;
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Ventilation in the neck is located at the junction of the neck and the base of the skull, and for this reason, it helps with constriction of the feet.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and with rupture of the windpipe, and with hoarseness, and with inflammation;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be pushed gently, for if it is held too tightly, it causes damage to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Ventilation at the .ij. ribs in the neck helps with headaches, and eye pain and migraine, and with strangulation, and toothache,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the area of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand when putting it in, so that he does not compress the artery and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation under the chin is good for mouth diseases and gum corruption and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the area of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation on the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Ventilation on the armpits is just as good as ventilation of the three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for beneath lies naked bone, and underneath that nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is placed on the buttock is useful for hemorrhoids and other diseases underneath, and it should be large, made of brass, and well-suctioning; and by chance, if it is fragile, it may break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very well, as they draw blood from the whole body; and they are useful for old pains in the kidneys, and for diseases of the stomach, and of the bladder, and they bring relief to flowers; and they are located at the .2nd sophene, and at the .2nd ankle, and all the while they weaken the body after a long time, and bring on fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is to place it first empty, and suck gently, and apply firmly, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the spot red and swollen, and the blood appears; then stop, and remove the cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have thin skin and wide pores: one must strike only once, and one must make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to subtilize the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then one must strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood a little at a time, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, then we must strike repeatedly; and if the blood is thick, then we strike it deeply, and the endings are such that the skin is pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it suits those who have thick and tough skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places where the cupping glasses will be placed with an opening and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in a state of inflammation, then use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in a state of suppuration, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the suppuration is thick and cold, then take marigold oil, or balsamite oil, or dill oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if those whom we heal have tender flesh and large pores, we must not put any oil on them.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but they must be washed afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should also use parsley, or water from the myrtle tree, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large swollen areas should use old wine, or water from the nettle plant, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or after the bath, but an hour or two hours after the bath; and do not sleep after bleeding.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he rest when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch out for those who are bilious, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is advisable to eat cool foods such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eating small fish, and meat from the bowels, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with cold complexions, take syrup of honey, and moderate sweet wine which is between old and new, and drink small birds and small fish;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he fasts, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people treacle or musk at certain times before or after fasting, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and dilute the wine, but it must not be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cupping glasses that are put without bleeding are those that are put on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the goiter, and on the belly and the udder and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not endure being bled on wounds,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as when we put them on the breasts when the nipples are sore; to reduce the swelling that is in a member, as when we put cupping glasses on the belly and udder to diminish the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	it removes pain when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it may remove the obstruction or draw the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it acts when placed upon the liver and spleen when there is retained flatulence,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to draw only, and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with warm water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 inches of width and a half palm depth, and on the sides all around the middle is a small hole like for pushing an awl through,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is made of iron, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle there is a crossbar made of iron or steel, for holding a candle in place,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and are both large and small according to the illnesses and ages of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and for the thin than for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must place this cupping glass on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the wax candle or the linen and place it inside the cupping glass through the tube that is inside the cupping glass,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the brightness is at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole that we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapors go in and out, and one removes the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and use the poultice as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup which is administered for disease of the pleurisy, in all aquosity, there is no tube or hole, and it is not used until it is filled with water, and is placed on the limb only empty.
et c’est li forme:	And this is how it is done:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are only applied outside of areas where cupping glasses cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on bare skin, such as the testicles or nipples, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of their use is that when you apply leeches that are in clean, clear water without any odor, they will take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and puts them in fresh water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then he should bleed them from a vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place leeches on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are swollen and itching, if there is a suitable spot to apply cupping, he should do so, for this brings great relief.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, he should raise the affected area, and then apply a poultice of ajuga, very well, and then express it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bite is too close to the body of the snake, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and apply it until the swelling goes down;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many bites, apply powdered vitriol or gall, and similar things, until the swelling goes down;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can put half a pod of peeled peas on the site and leave them until they turn green; this will stop the swelling immediately;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, catch other snakes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the fresh wound with blood, or insert a needle so that the leech can suck out the blood.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on top, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are sucking, then powder with a mixture of aloe and salt, or ashes, and they will stop immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish people think this chapter comes from nowhere but their own heads, and that they have never read about it in any ancient books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason the knowledge of medicine is strange in our land, for I have found no good ones among them.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing about it except through the study of ancient books, through which I have acquired the knowledge and through experimentation and the habits of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained within, and summarized it at the end, and clearly demonstrated the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in the two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the subjects of the discourse and the chapters where the sage sets his understanding, and dwells on their truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twisting, or broken bones occur to anyone, you should quickly treat the patient from both sides, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or age, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is very hot or very cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cool jellies, and deer and hare meat, and do not drink any wine, nor consume any fatty foods, and do not fill himself with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have suspected a hot abscess or material swelling in the affected limb; then let the patient return to their previous course of treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, then one should nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and cow's placenta, and offal, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such swelling the fracture is stopped up and heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be well mended or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but have no worry, reset the broken bone with a large tendon that joins and holds the member together, forcing it as it was before; and do not stop all of its function, and for this reason it must be nourished with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another one that is superficial, just like the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a complete fracture is a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each dislocation there is its own method and proper instrument for restoration, depending on what comes to mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the fracture of the bone is known by its being twisted and clearly visible through the skin, and it sounds hollow when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting and no sound when touched, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But there may still be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply remedies that follow, then hold it steady with a gentle grip.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and are the two disjoined parts, they must now be put back in place evenly, so that hot abscesses do not come from it;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, let them be for a day or two until the abscesses are settled;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then reset it as evenly as you can lightly and gently, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it steady, as appropriate, as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, it is to be set with two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are set, you must reset them with all your strength in their places as much as you can, and be careful that your action does not cause the patient injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two heads of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it does not seem right; then adjust it well, and do not pull or press too hard as those do who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the member through their actions, as we have seen many times.Et s’il est desaloiee par cause de moistor ou de fureur, si le ramene en sa leu, et il ne puet y demorer, si le remet a leu si com il doit etre;
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is healed, then carefully instruct the patient not to move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the member is so secure that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then he is not healed, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be sure that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as fingers, toes, and the like: in these cases, one should use soft, thin linen wraps.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for larger members, such as the arm and leg: one should use a wide, sturdy wrap, as a wide wrap encompasses the entire large member and constrains it evenly all around, so that there is no pressure point.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tightly wrap the joint with light bandages, three or four turns depending on the member, and hold your hand firmly against all of the ligament for a moment, then go above the dislocation and press less hard, so that the dislocation is moved slightly away from the joint;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	then soften the ligament little by little, until you press on most of the healthy area, then take hold of another ligament, and go around the dislocated joint again;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the dislocation, and press gently, not too hard or too softly, as we have said above in the first ligament;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages of linen or cloth, until they are all even, then bind everything tightly with a bandage, and then put your splints on well-made, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something hot that soothes the abscess and reduces the swelling for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then press down with your fingers, and let them be made of half a thick cane, or of wood that chisels are made from, or of palm tree branches, and let them be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the finger placed on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as it needs to be for the small or large limb;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it against the stars just as you did at first, then tie a thread over it gently, just as in the case of a fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is held, the less it will move; and the thread must be neither too thin nor too thick, but of medium thickness, and made from soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen fools make their knots with twisted flaxen cords, and this is a great error, for the knot cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than a finger's width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded on the head by the stars after the binding, place underneath woolen or linen bandages so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not attempt to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when a limb is large, it should not be set until after five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the method for ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations and torsion: You should take flour from the walls of the mill and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method for a poultice to restore fractures in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to restore the fracture and dislocation and twisting: take 3 parts rose oil, 1 part each of myrrh and aloe, 8 parts alechi, and in powder, mix with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is suitable for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is useful for twisting: take myrrh and viscovium, each 10 parts; aloe and acacia, each 6 parts; Armenian bole 10 parts, and grind well, and cook in water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their sockets, and to ease the resulting pain, and to smooth the bone, and for fractures: take new lamb's wool, and moisten it in arsenical oil and cook it, and apply it to the affected area. This plaster does not heal, but it is good for easing hot abscesses and removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster from it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of ointment for the restoration of the fracture of the bone and to reduce the remainder of the abscess. Take the root of marsh mallow, chamomile, violets, wheat flour, each one part; and bruise, and cook in wine, and if the member is hot, cook it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of ointment stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take the roots of marsh mallow, and flax seed, borage, sweet-clover, and sanicle, and violets and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; and bruise, and cook in salt water or sweet water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member to restore it other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and too hard.Et dist qu’on doit prendre la cerote en la meine et la mettre sus le membre, et la faire adurer a la manie dou feu, si come l’huile chaude, et la mettre sus la brisure.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one must put on the broken member, in order to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and beaver castoreum, and mix them together, and grind them up, and make an ointment out of it, and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if so, loosen it again after several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the area, or discomfort or swelling, then be quick about it and loosen it, and remove the ointment; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea water, and dip it in water, and wipe the affected area with it, until the itching stops and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage, until you are sure of the hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and soothe the inflammation of the limb, and take away the pain, then restart the gentle binding, and a little ointment, and do not bind it as tightly as before; gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess is red and painful and swollen all around, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, then do not loosen it until after 3, or 4, or 5, or 7 days; and sometimes let it be for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and the bone draws near to the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then restrain it more than before, and increase his food, as I said earlier; and if you see the site drying out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then give him warm water to drink, every time you release him, and do this three times a day, and ease the pressure slightly each time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work, the healing comes to the limb, and quickly diminishes what the foolish doctors do, who restore the limb crookedly: it is harmful, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing in it but laziness and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaking methods
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are fractures that are caused by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone is broken all the way to the shoulder joint, just like a spear or staff; and this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts into the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a closed fracture, or a split, or from the collarbone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a deep fracture that approaches the membrane below the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the fracture is lodged in the bone as delicately as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by stone or by falling, or in a similar way, and forces the bone fragment inward, and the site is hairy like the blacksmith when they work on kettles; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist skull bones, as in children's skulls;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and happens with all these types of fractures, that small pieces are dislodged as they are; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of fractures through examination, and through the corruption that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by the fact that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it with a finger, the fracture appears black.Si li os est fraiz et tuit contuz, et n’a nul semblant de brisure, ne conoissons pas s’il y a brisure si nous ne veons la sanguine qui s’en va ou s’en vient; car la sanguine qui s’en va, ne li dislocatiers ne se guarient si tost.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of signs of infection in the patient, and if you see any malicious accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes bulging and reddening, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.Et si li os est contuz et rompu, et li brisure n’est point noire ne sanguine ne s’en va; et les accidens dou malaide ne sont pas sus; et li os est en son leu, et la dislocation est guariee, si covient que tu esprouves li os se il est tuit en son leu; car il adonques n’y a nul semblant de brisure, si li os est contuz.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a dreadful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the child comes to you for the first time, and it is in winter, then you must remove the tooth before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you must hurry to remove the tooth before the seventh day, otherwise, the gum under the tooth will be corrupted and the accidents that we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus: and it is that you grip the head of the patient with the mouth open wide, and expose the bone in every way you can, and at the level of the wound more than you can,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows when discovering the bone, or if an abscess forms, assist using what is appropriate, and you should fill the area with wet rags soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed and bleeding stopped; then begin around the bone to remove it, and there are two ways of doing this. One way is to cut narrowly in front, which is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then cut another larger slit than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have various slits, some narrow and some wide, pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it so that you can administer cauteries with tongs without breaking through the bone into the chest cavity; above the tip there should be a rim or a ring that prevents the tip from going beyond the bone. You should have several of these, so that each one goes in at the level of the thickness of the bone, and you will need tongs for all parts of the body. There are three types of tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The technique for piercing around a broken bone is to place one tong on the bone and twist it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the tong to another spot a little further along, and do this all around. Then cut away the bone between the piercings as precisely and gently as you can, as we have said, until you can pull the bone out by hand or with instruments such as pliers or tweezers; be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and loosened the bone, it is necessary to remove the membrane that is still attached to the bone with any suitable instrument like an incision knife, but it should be thinner and more flexible than the other knives.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there is anything left of the small bones or scales, remove them with instruments; then treat the wound as we have said, with bandages and ointments.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen speaks of, which is safer; he praises it highly, and it is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you should expose a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place under the head of this lens-shaped instrument, of which there is one made especially for this purpose:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not cut on one side, but the part is pointed in two places, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then hit it gently with a small mallet, so that you slightly chip the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is glued to the bone, loosen it gently, for bones are loosened without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the shards with a thin rasp, of which you should have various quantities, in order to apply in each place what is most appropriate, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take the largest rasp first, then one that is more subtle, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.
