In each of the other subtle hair-like fractures and breaks, you should treat according to its nature; and this is something that has not been handed down to one who has devoted his studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinus is exposed, then you should spread a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the wound, then apply another ligature over it, and do not tighten it more than necessary so that it only presses against the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like this for one or two days until the abscesses are soothed, then remove the ligature, and apply medicine such as lily roots, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and then apply other medicine without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and be careful that the wound is clean and dry so that you do not leave any ointment or pus, because when pus gathers under the skin, it will fester and cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the wound, it will fester underneath.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine that has been applied, for such a virtue it should have, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and with it glue one piece of cloth and place it over the ulcer;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the jaw above are broken, either one or the other, for they are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break but only becomes dislocated or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must push your little finger or finger into the hole of the jaw, and put that broken part inside your index finger and hold it there until the jaw returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper jaw and the tooth cannot return to its place, then you should put it back into alignment with a thin tool.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if it is a double fracture, do the same, and try to restore it on the first day if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have healed, then put on a head bandage made of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you can use a cautery of fire, if the break is there; and let the tent be so large that it fills the holes in the nails.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some say that one should moisten the tent with butter, and change it every day. I do not think this is good, but one should moisten it while preparing egg white, and flour from the mill; then leave the tent as long as the bone is stiff, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they insert the quills of goose feathers in place of tents, and tie a silk cloth around it, and hold it in place, and the patient blows through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if painful abscesses come to the nails while you are working there, then put a poultice of cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a pouch of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if no pus comes out, then apply a plaster made from flour of mallow leaves, and powdered incense, cooked in egg white, then place on top light sponges, but do not bind it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments for this purpose, then cut the wound, and treat it with healing substances that are warm and soft, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in splints of plaster, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	On dislocation of the jaw:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is completely dislocated and there is no open wound, and the dislocation is only on the surface, and not broken in two where the corbels are inside, then it can be easily identified.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if it's on the left side of the jaw, use your right hand's index finger, and gently push the dislocation back into place with your other hand, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the dislocation of the jaw is to one side, you must administer an extension of two parts, so that it is equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the teeth, or a dislocation, then he should be restrained with a gold or silver or silk thread, and then put cerate on the jaw, and put over it two layers of cloth; and put on top of the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather as long and wide as the jaw, and tie it tightly according to how he can bear it, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and apply an ointment made of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or flour of sisament, after you have removed the cerote; and apply another light ointment on top, and if the ointments hurt, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed; many are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine carefully to see if any piece of bone has been removed; then remove it skillfully using appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, then loosen it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains nothing, then stitch the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is cured.
de la forcele	of the scrotum
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The scrotum may rupture in several ways, towards the shoulder, and there are three types of rupture: one where it is ruptured and separated into two pieces, which is the least serious and can be easily repaired; another where there is a rupture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is, when there is no wound with the rupture, to have two assistants: one holds the scrotum where it is ruptured, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then use your fingers to bring the edges of the rupture together so that the shape is correct, with no gaps or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round pillow made of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your needs; then hold steady the arm and press the pillow in your hand so that you set the break evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the arm out of its socket because it is deeply lodged, then the patient should lie on his back, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and the assistant pushes the shoulder upwards while pulling the arm down so that the bone of the arm is dislocated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then adjust the break with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you should split it open; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, then cut into one of the incisions that you have made, but place this instrument under the arm to protect the skin:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and is shaped like a spoon, and has no sharp edges, and is as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the extent of the wound; and has .ij. edges, as you can see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, just as the edge of the wound that you made when you pulled the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt it is a hot abscess, then pack the wound with bandages and poultices according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses arise, moisten a bandage in rosemary oil and garlic and wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dislocation of bones, when there is no wound or cut, is treated by applying a poultice of millpowder and egg white to the bone, and placing light compresses on top. If necessary, place a wooden splint underneath the joint.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage, about the width of a palm, and place a double bandage on top of the compresses and poultice. Then take a thin staff, three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the splint over the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy collarbone, and under the collarbone on the affected side; and reset it from each direction, and when you see that the ligament is holding the fracture in place properly, and you can clearly see that the splint is not moving over the broken bone, then release it each day, and when the ligature slacks, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and let the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the collarbone to raise the shoulder, so that the fracture will be pulled upwards by the weight of the arm; then release the bandage around the neck, and tie the arm to the neck if no bad event happens, until 20 days have passed.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the poultice if you see that it is needed, and keep doing this until he is healed; and it will be healed within 28 days, but some people recover sooner than others.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Here, the shoulder is broken or dislocated, and it is not felt except by touch; then adjust the apparatus according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in every way you can; then apply powdered flour with egg white over the affected area, and light dressings, and place a double sheet over that; then place a broad, thin pillow, slightly larger than the shoulder, on top, and if there is any swelling under the pillow on the shoulder, pack that area with linen dressings so that the pillow lies evenly; then bind it firmly with a wide bandage so that the pillow does not move from its position, and check the binding every day; and whenever it becomes loose, bind it again, and adjust the pillow if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this period is complete, loosen the bandage, and be careful, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes outward and not downward into the chest, make an incision and remove the bone, and do what we have said about healing a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	about the fracture of the foot:
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but that seldom happens; it often breaks at the tip. And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks downward, and the patient experiences great pain, and loses his sexual desire, and feels cold all over, and may vomit blood, and the break shows through the skin of the broken bone, and he feels it himself.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring the two sides of the ribs together with your hands, pushing gently to ensure they are even; then apply poultices and bandages made from salt or some other light material over the broken bone, and tie it in place so it does not move; then wrap the whole area in a cloth, and keep checking every hour, loosening the ligature if it becomes too tight, and changing the poultice regularly to treat any infections, pruritus, pain, or abscesses that may develop; once the bone is healed, remove the poultice and bandages, and address any scarring with appropriate remedies.
de la brisure des costes	about the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You should know that rib fractures only occur in the upper back near the spine, and they do not bend unless they are slippery; and it feels good when pressed on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then the restoration is to put the broken bone back in place, as it should be. And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone punctures the lung; and they have shortness of breath, and cough up, and vomit a great quantity of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the elderly have died from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make the fire, that hot embers won't come from it, if they didn't come from it.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place cupping glasses over the area to draw out fluids, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cupping glasses will attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wet woolen cloth soaked in warm oil, and place tents between the ribs to ensure even pressure all around; then it should be treated with pleurisy-cures made from meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone piercing through the tent, and there is doubt about the condition, then one should split the skin over the broken rib, and place a padding underneath to protect the pleura; then one should saw through the bone, pulling gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, treating it with poultices until it heals. If hot abscesses form, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil over the area; treat the area around the abscess as needed, keeping the patient lying on their side where it is most comfortable, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the bones in the neck, and it doesn't bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will survive or not, take note: if you see their hands soft, swollen, and lifeless, and they cannot move or straighten them, and when you prick them with a needle, they don't feel it. Know that it is deadly in many cases; but if they can move their hands and feel the pain when you stretch or press on them, know that the joint is saved, and the injury will heal if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if this happens to the spine in the back, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note: if their feet are swollen, and they have similar symptoms in their hands, and they pass gas and defecate without wanting to; and when they are lain on their stomach, they pass gas without wanting to. And when they are lain on their back and they want to sit up, they cannot. Know that it is deadly: if there is no progress in their treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the case is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, then the doctor should put rosemary oil or hen's egg white on it until it is soothed; then he should apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bandage it, and instruct the patient to rest; and he should not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is exposed, then it should be covered with a bandage; and the bone is removed, then the two lips of the wound are sewed together, if it is large, with a single stitch, and the doctor applies ointment and a plaster, if necessary; and he instructs the patient to keep it pressed, and if there is an exposed bone, they should press on it, remove it, treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Then the bones of the hip are broken, and if they are, then there is usually some lessening in the upper part; and it hurts a lot, and declines toward the perineum, and brings pain to the area, and punctures, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the break; and know which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only in the upper part, then make that break even, so that it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then let the patient lie on his stomach, so that the restoration of that break is prepared for him.Et s’il est dou lonc et decline au pardedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son dos, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, then put on the plaster, and then put on a board or splint, and bind the break so that it does not move; and apply the area under the ribs, so that the collarbone is made even.Et s’il avient que la brisure soit au chief soulement, si met le malaide sus son dos, et li estele soulement sus l’emplaustre, et li lieure desoz les costes, et li brisure adessous.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a boil erupts, do not touch it until the boil is suppurated, and apply what we have mentioned earlier; then return to restoration, and constrict as needed if there is no bad outcome; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the .ii. ways: one of which is that you take a plain stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two feet with two ropes, and they can be pulled up, and the patient is seated on a chair; then he lowers his broken arm onto the beam until it reaches the ground, and puts a curve in the beam, then pulls it down over some heavy object or the minister stretches it downward; then put the mirror at an angle equal to his hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to suspend the patient from his harness, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two ministers, one to pull up what is above the break to his hands, and the other to pull down under the entire rope, and each pulls on their own side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tie one rope under the break and another above it, and each minister pulls on their own side. And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must put a light rope under the joint, and another toward the elbow, under the break; and likewise, if the break is toward the elbow, then tie a light rope gently without effort so that the break is equal on the joint and toward the elbow; then put the mirror at an angle equal to his hands together, so that the break returns as it should, and tie it tightly if no abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a deep abscess comes, do not drain it until the 7th day, and place soft linen in ash and rose oil on the abscess, so that the deep abscess is relieved; then drain it, and the manner of draining it is to place the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm over the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and place a cloth, and drain it over the shoulder, and over the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing moves it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints and place a splint larger and stronger than the others over the fracture, and have 1 inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends 3 inches on either side of the fracture; then drain over the splints, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter over the fracture, more strongly and less by pulling.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the settling of the splints and the drainage, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it be bound until the 7th day, as we have said; then look at the bandage every 3 days to see if itching or swelling comes to the site, or if suppuration can come to the member because it is too tight. If so, loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come, then do not loosen it for three days or more; let the patient sleep on his back and keep his hands on his stomach; place underneath the shoulder a plain woolen cushion, and every hour of the day or night, check that the broken limb does not move or the ligature become soft; then treat him with medicine and give him food as we have already described, so that the food is in its most subtle form first; when he begins to recover, then make it thick. It is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset within 40 days; then loosen it and administer baths and ointment treatments to ease the pain. And if the dislocation is severe and swollen, leave it for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	from the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones called the 'ulna', one of which is small and located near the armpit, and the other is large and located below the small bone towards the little finger; sometimes only the large ulna is fractured, or the small one, and sometimes both are broken.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing are easy; but when the large ones are broken, their healing is difficult, and they cause more pain than when they were both broken together. If it is only a small bone that is broken, then it should be gently straightened and set even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone, then it should be pulled harder; and extend it onto a cushion, and tie the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves, and place a cushion in front of them so that they do not feel any pain; then extend the minister's arm under the affected area to his hand, or to the other one above it. And then set the mirror even according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are broken pieces, place each one in its proper location; and if any stick out, grab the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before regarding the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken of it in the individual chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, pustules occur, then apply .i. cloth of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and place .i. cloth over it gently, so that the pustules are soothed. And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of the powder of the mill with the yolk of an egg, then put the bandages, and let the bandage on the fracture be stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have six bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or both; and press more on the fracture than elsewhere, and every day less, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And then inspect the member and the bandages after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes on it, then you must moisten the member with warm water so that this itching is relieved; and do not let the member remain tight, but loosen it. And then restart the binding, and if the bandages become loose and the bone slips out of place, or anything similar happens, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care so that the healing cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little, and let it be thus for several days, until the healing occurs, and then bind it again.Et se li maux sont de la guareine, si covient que tu le tiens estreit et que tu l’esprenges de vne uie chaude, et li pons  .i. drapeil de cerote, et li pons  .i. drapeil de la poudre dou molin, et puis li pons les esteles, si com nos avons dit davant; et laisse li maux venir au membre, et ne li esprenges mie; et se il vient au membre, si covient que tu l’esprenges, et li tiens le membre estreit.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days have passed or a little more, then he can move his hands to his neck and keep his neck even, and guard against movement and straining, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed within thirty days, or perhaps within twenty days, according to the combinations of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and around the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from many折ures.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should lean forward, and then he should extend his hand and stretch out his fingers, and then the minister should reset any displaced bones and align them correctly; and if there are no abscesses, then they should apply a plaster and bandages according to the size of the injury, and then wrap it in a single piece of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the stomach of the plant, make a sphere out of cloth, and instruct the patient to grip it with their broken hand; then hold it with a long piece of cloth, and let the mark of the burn be as big as the palm of the hand, and hold it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside of the hand, you should place one splint above and another below the hand, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, such as the thumb, set it straight, as it should be; and hold it with the palm, and see if you can place a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in any other finger, such as the index or another, set it straight as well, and bind the injured finger with the one next to it; or you can bind them all together while keeping them straight, or you can place a splint on top, as in the case of the thumb; and take care in the restoration and preparation of a hot abscess, and treat any pus that forms, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken and this can be seen when it is bent forward and backward; its restoration depends on binding with a bandage above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And let the patient lie on his back, then extend each bandage to its respective part equally; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one bandage should go towards the buttock and the other under the break. And similarly, if it is near the knee, then the bandage should go past the knee and the extension should be directed downward; then the surgeon should align the bone with his two hands as best he can to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and the bandage, unless an abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down first and then return to your work and treatment; the time frame is as follows.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap the fracture with a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and leave it for the surplus, then return the leg so that the heels come to the root of the toe, and thread a long piece of string between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the string come out above; then go back up the leg and over the thigh with the bandage, then place splints on the fracture, and put one splint on top of the bone of the leg; then tie the space between the leg and the thigh with soft fabric to even out the pressure, then start tying three or four turns around the fracture firmly; the more you go up from the fracture, the less you should tighten it; then feel the two pieces of string that you threaded between the thigh and the leg, and tie three splints that are on top, then go back down to the end of the string, so that you reach the foot; tighten it so that it doesn't move from its place, then leave it as it is so that no abscess, swelling, or anything else comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens, remove it and treat what happened as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone protruding, they should be removed if possible; and if not, the area should be split open and cleaned out; and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.Et s’il i a aposteme ou enfleure, si le deslie et adrecce la briseure, si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken as if by stars, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, such restoration does not help the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little less or more, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	You should know that there is little breaking of the knee, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and it happens to all, with or without pain, and everyone feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal to what is torn in his hands, as long as they can be assembled; then put the plaster, and if necessary, place a round splint, and tighten it as needed; then observe all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar conditions; and apply to each occurrence what is appropriate, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You should know that in the leg there are 2 bones, one of which is properly called the "tibia", and the other is called the "fibula"; and all kinds of fractures occur in it as they do in the arm, and so the restoration is the same as that for the arm, and the procedures are the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are fractured together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, return above.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, there will be great pain and it can be seen; then go below. Therefore, apply extension and make it even, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is disfigured and there are multiple pieces, the extension should be lighter and more gentle; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two wooden splints which support the leg on both sides from the knee down to below it; then wind two bandages around them above and below, and tie it in the middle, and at this time the leg should not be able to bend to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some use a board as long as the leg, and they put the leg on it to guard against movement, and properly they make that which is in the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; then treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot and toes, and nothing more than a sprain in various locations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot, and you see the bones rising above one another, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, at the point where the bones are raised; then press it so hard that they return to their proper position. Then apply the ointment and bandages, and underneath the sole of the foot, place a small wooden board with two flat sides, then tighten it securely around the foot, and wrap cloth and other materials around it as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find that the bones are healed, whether they were fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there is any broken bone in the foot, treat it as we have described for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be slightly larger; then place underneath the foot that wooden board which I mentioned earlier, and tighten it securely; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, place on top of each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let the top of the board press firmly against the sole of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures; and treat each case as it arises.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's wrist are broken, have her sit with her back bent forward, and hold her from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and insert a stone as large as a bean; then make the woman stand up, and gently lift her back up little by little, and the cotton will come out with the stone as it returns to its natural place. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, put it back in, and do this for seven days; the fracture will be healed. Then take a goat's bladder, attach a tube to the opening, and fill the bladder with air by blowing into the tube until it is inflated inside the wound; the natural place will return to its original position. Fill the wound with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bones of the wrist of a man or woman are broken, treat it as we have described for the hip bone; these fractures are not hidden from those who dedicate themselves to its study and practice, and who understand my book. For the fractures indicate in various ways the right path to restoration; listen therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When a penis is broken, take a goose's throat and insert it into the penis; then wrap it tightly with cloth, leave it for three days or until it heals, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	from breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated immediately, and the treatments that we have described bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, and there is no sign of infection, then you should restart the treatment for the break in the same hour or that day, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if painful abscesses arise, let the healing wait until the next day, so that the abscesses are soothed, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about an evil event.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed chest, you should gently put it in place with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you for putting it in place with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width depends on the amount of the wound; and it requires the surgeon to grasp it three or four times, depending on each case of broken bone; and it should be round and a bit thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and thin at the front, and thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a «palainche», so that the curved shoulder should be placed on the head of the apparent bone; and bend it once, as far as it will go, and make it even with the other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you should cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut into it with an appropriate tool, or a scalpel or saw, to your ability; then remove that which is lodged in the bone, with roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. Then do as much as you can to put it back into its proper place, then moisten a cloth with black wine vinegar, and apply it carefully if there is swelling; and do not put any ointment or other medicine on the wound that would cause pus and corruption; then bandage the wound after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the bandage around the entire wound, according to its size, and be careful that the wound is not restricted by the bandage; and many times fools have done this and caused their patients to suffer pain or even death; and the dislocation should be looser and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is large or deep, and you doubt that harm may come to it, as we have said, and there is pain in the area, then do not put anything on top of the bandages; but wrap around, instead of the bandages, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after a day or two pus forming at the wound, remove what you have placed on top to the very bottom, and apply ointment that heals wounds, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ointments.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and mended.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary for the limb to be positioned in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days, and it cannot be souded but keeps dislocating the bowstring, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you should probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these dislocated pieces which cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula or other form of corruption appears, then it should be treated according to what he says in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, as with the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not splint it, because many die from this, but leave it until it can be healed; perhaps it will fall off after 20 or 30 days; then cure the wound if you can, and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruises that come over the soudure
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	After the fracture, many things come to the surface, especially when it is near the joint; and it is an ugly sight to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	So take care that the pus is brought to the surface: so the minister to him astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others; or you grind some of these things, or all together, and confit them with wine astringent, or with vinegar of eggs, or with garlic; and put it on the wound at night in poultices, and tie it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen it, and start another one, until the knot is removed; or you apply it to a piece of plaster well made; for the property of plaster is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the knot has turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, scrape it off, and bring the superfluity to the surface; or you have it removed by someone skilled in shaving, so that it is removed, and the wound is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of profuse bleeding; or because of excessive movement, and not at the right time; or because there is little blood in his body, and it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, so that the blood multiplies in him; and the minister gives him a bath, and gives him joy and relaxation; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts a great deal of heat, and often washes it with tepid water, so that the heat runs into the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	then the limb becomes straight after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb again completely, and many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm, and even death can come from them; nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, then they should be washed with hot water, or soft herbs are cooked, such as leaves of mullein, and roots, and marsh-mallow, and similar medicines that soften; and you make an emollient, such as a well-made diaquilon, and you take the mucilage of mullein, and infuse it with tallow or sisam oil, and apply it as an ointment; or you take fat figs, and grind them with colon-fibre, and similar medicines.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the dislocation is relieved by rubbing continually and repeatedly with moist hands; and movement is applied to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosities are awake and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove them with iron, then one must cut them down to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and put cotton and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one must immediately reset it without delay.
